Ruling on Ruined Waqf Property: When Does It Revert?
Ruling on waqf property that becomes completely unusable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a waqf property that becomes completely unusable and identify the conditions for its reversion or treatment as luqtah.

Core Idea
A completely ruined waqf property reverts to the founder or becomes luqtah.

The sanctity of waqf is such that property is dedicated eternally to Allah. But what happens when the property is utterly destroyed and cannot be used? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses that rare but critical scenario, providing a ruling that balances the intention of the founder with practical reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal situation? A waqf property (shop or tank) that is completely ruined and cannot be benefited from or repaired. The ruling: it reverts to the waqf-founder or his heirs.
The ruin must be total, not partial.
2
Locate the condition for reversion
The condition is that the property is 'such that it cannot be benefited from nor rented at all' and 'cannot be repaired'. If any benefit remains, it stays waqf.
The text gives examples: a burnt shop and a ruined tank.
3
Note the procedure when heirs are unknown
If the waqf-founder and heirs are unknown, the property is treated as 'luqtah' (lost property). It is given in charity to a poor person, who then sells it and uses the price.
This is from Fatawa al-Khasi.
4
Consider the dissenting view
Al-Sadr al-Shahid questioned this ruling because waqf is dedicated to Allah and should not return to human ownership. The author notes that the full discussion will come later.
This shows internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما في الذخيرة وغيرها : حانوت احترق في السوق وصار بحيث لا ينتفع به ولا يستأجر ألبتة وحوض محلة خرب وصار بحال لا يمكن عمارته فهو للواقف ولورثته، فإن كان واقفه وورثته لا تعرف فهو لقطة زاد في فتاوى الخاصي : إذا كان كاللقطة يتصدقون به على فقير ثم يبيعه الفقير فينتفع بثمنه فقال الصدر الشهيد في جنس هذه المسائل نظر يعني لأن الوقف بعدما خرج إلى الله تعالى لا يعود إلى ملك الواقف وسيأتي تمامه في بيان شروط الواقف عند قوله وإن شرط الولاية لنفسه».
And as for what is in al-Dhakhirah and others: a shop that burnt in the market and became such that it cannot be benefited from nor rented at all, and a tank of a neighborhood that became ruined and became in a state that cannot be repaired, it belongs to the waqf-founder and his heirs. If its waqf-founder and his heirs are unknown, it is lost property. Added in Fatawa al-Khasi: if it is like lost property, they give it in charity to a poor person, then the poor person sells it and benefits from its price. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said about this type of issues: there is consideration, meaning because the waqf after it has gone out to Allah does not return to the ownership of the waqf-founder, and its completion will come in the conditions of the waqf-founder at his statement 'and if he stipulates the guardianship for himself'.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage rules on a waqf property that has become completely useless. If a shop burns and cannot be used or rented, or a water tank becomes ruined and cannot be repaired, the property goes back to the waqf-founder or his heirs. If they are unknown, it is treated as lost property (luqtah). According to Fatawa al-Khasi, it is given in charity to a poor person who then sells it and uses the price. However, al-Sadr al-Shahid questions this because once property is made waqf, it is dedicated to Allah and should not return to ownership. The author notes that this issue will be discussed later.

Key Terms
لقطة (luqṭah): Lost property found by someone else; in this context, a ruined waqf property with unknown founder/heirs is treated as lost property to be given in charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a ruined waqf tank if the waqf-founder and his heirs are unknown?
A) It remains waqf for future use.
B) It is given to the ruler.
C) It is treated as lost property (luqtah).
D) It is sold and the money given to the state.

Key Takeaway
A completely ruined waqf property reverts to its founder or heirs; if unknown, it is treated as luqtah.

Mutawalli Purchasing Property from Mosque Income: Conditions and Dispute
Ruling on mutawalli buying property from mosque income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a mutawalli may purchase property from mosque income and explain the difference of opinion regarding the subsequent sale of that property.

Core Idea
A mutawalli may purchase income-generating property with mosque surplus, but only with the judge's permission; the bought property's waqf status is disputed.

In Hanafi fiqh, the mutawalli (trustee) of a mosque is responsible for managing its assets and using its income for the mosque's benefit. A key question arises: can the mutawalli use surplus income to buy new property (e.g., a shop or house) as an investment? Two classical Hanafi works, al-Khaniyyah and al-Qunyah, provide guidance on this issue, including a difference of opinion on whether such purchased property becomes part of the mosque waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
Consider the mutawalli (trustee) and the act of purchasing property using income generated from mosque waqf.
2
Determine the default ruling
According to al-Khaniyyah, the purchase is permissible because it serves the mosque's interests.
3
Identify the condition for validity
Al-Qunyah adds that such a purchase requires the permission of the judge (qadi); the mutawalli's general authority does not include buying property.
4
Analyze the disagreement on selling the purchased property
Some scholars say the purchased property becomes waqf and cannot be sold; others say it remains ordinary property because no waqf declaration was made.
5
Determine the authoritative ruling
The text declares the second view correct (wa huwa al-sahīh): the property is not waqf, so it can be sold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : المتولي إذا اشترى من غلة المسجد حانوتاً أو داراً أو مستغلاً آخر جاز لأن هذا من مصالح المسجد، فإن أراد المتولي أن يبيع ما اشترى أو باع اختلفوا فيه ؛ قال بعضهم: يجوز هذا البيع لأن هذا صار من أوقاف المسجد. وقال بعضهم : يجوز هذا البيع وهو الصحيح لأن المشتري لم يذكر شيئاً من شرائط الوقف فلا يكون ما اشترى من جملة أوقاف المسجد ا هـ . وفي القنية : إنما يجوز الشراء بإذن القاضي لأنه لا يستفاد الشراء من مجرد تفويض القوامة إليه فلو استدان في ثمنه وقع الشراء له اهـ
And in al-Khaniyyah: The mutawalli, if he buys from the income of the mosque a shop or a house or another income-generating property, it is permissible because this is from the interests of the mosque. If the mutawalli wants to sell what he bought or sold, they differed about it; some said: this sale is permissible because this has become part of the mosque endowments. And some said: this sale is permissible and it is the correct view because the buyer did not mention any of the conditions of waqf, so what he bought is not from the total of the mosque endowments. And in al-Qunyah: The purchase is only permissible with the permission of the judge because the purchase is not derived from mere delegation of guardianship to him. If he borrows for its price, the purchase is for him.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from Hanafi sources. First, from al-Khaniyyah: A mutawalli (administrator) of a mosque can use mosque income (such as from rental of waqf properties) to buy new income-generating property (like a shop or house) for the mosque's benefit. This is allowed. However, if the mutawalli then wants to sell that purchased property, there is a difference of opinion. Some say it has become part of the mosque waqf and cannot be sold. Others say it is not part of the waqf because no formal declaration of waqf was made, so selling is allowed. The second opinion is deemed correct. Second, from al-Qunyah: Such a purchase requires the permission of the judge because the mutawalli's authority to manage does not automatically include the right to buy property. If the mutawalli borrows money to pay the price, the purchased property belongs to him personally, not the mosque.

Key Terms
متولي (mutawallī): The administrator or trustee of a waqf.
غلة المسجد (ghullat al-masjid): Income generated from mosque waqf properties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Qunyah, when is a mutawalli allowed to purchase property from mosque income?
A) Without any condition
B) With permission of the judge
C) With permission of the congregation
D) Only if the property is a house

Key Takeaway
A mutawalli may only purchase property from mosque income with the judge's permission, and the purchased property does not automatically become waqf.

Non-Division of Waqf and Housing Rights of Beneficiaries
Ruling that waqf property is not divided among beneficiaries, with details on housing rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that waqf property cannot be divided among beneficiaries and apply the rules for housing rights when space is limited.

Core Idea
Waqf corpus remains undivided; beneficiaries only share usufruct, not ownership.

This lesson explains the foundational Hanafi principle that waqf property is not subject to division among its beneficiaries. While beneficiaries have rights to the usufruct, they cannot partition the corpus. The text then applies this principle to a common scenario: a house made waqf for dwelling, outlining the rules for co-residence, spousal access, and the prohibition on charging rent even when space is tight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State that the waqf property is not divided among the beneficiaries, even if they are the founder's children.
This is a prohibition on division: the act of dividing is legally invalid (batil).
2
Understand the rationale
Beneficiaries have no right to the corpus (al-ayn); they only have a right to the income/usufruct (al-ghullah).
This distinguishes waqf from inheritance or shared ownership.
3
Apply to the housing branch
If a house is made waqf for dwelling, it cannot be divided among the beneficiaries; they share the dwelling proportionately.
Even if the house becomes crowded, they do not have the right to partition or rent out extra space.
4
Handle crowding and spousal rights
If there are separate rooms, each beneficiary may house their spouse; if not, no apportionment occurs. Beneficiaries may only lend space for free, not rent.
Muhayā'ah (time-sharing) is not allowed; the dwelling is for those specifically named.
5
Note the consequence of occupation
If some occupy more space, the others cannot demand rent; they may request to share the space or the constrained party must leave or sit adjacent.
This reinforces that no financial compensation is due for differential use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يقسم وإن وقفه على أولاده) أي لا يقسم الموقوف بين مستحقيه ولو كانوا أولاد الواقف لأنه لا حق لهم في العين وإنما حقهم في الغلة. وفي فتح القدير : وأجمعوا أن الكل لو كان وقفاً على الأرباب وأرادوا القسمة لا يجوز التهايؤ وعليه فرع ما لو وقف داره على سكنى قوم بأعيانهم أو ولده ونسله أبداً ما تناسلوا فإذا انقرضوا كانت غلتها للمساكين فإن هذا الوقف جائز على هذا الشرط، وإذا انقرضوا تكرى وتوضع غلتها للمساكين وليس لأحد من الموقوف عليهم السكنى أن يكتريها ولو زادت على قدر حاجة سكناه نعم له الإعارة لا غير. ولو كثر أولاد هذا الواقف وولد ولده ونسله ضاقت الدار عليهم ليس لهم إلا سكناها تقسط على عددهم. ولو كانوا ذكوراً وإناثاً، حتى إن كان فيها حجر ومقاصير كان للذكور أن يسكنوا نساءهم معهم وللنساء أن يسكن أزواجهن معهن، وإن لم يكن فيها حجر لا يستقيم أن تقسم بينهم ولا يقع فيها مهايأة إنما سكناها لمن جعل الواقف له ذلك لا لغيرهم. وعن هذا يعرف أنه لو سكن بعضهم فلم يجد الآخر موضعاً يكفيه لا يستوجب الآخر أجرة حصته على الساكنين بل إن أحب أن يسكن معه في بقعة من تلك الدار بلا زوجة أو زوج إن كان لأحدهم ذلك وإلا ترك المتضيق وخرج أو جلسوا معاً كل في بقعة إلى جنب الآخر. والأصل المذكور في الشروح الفرع في أوقاف الخصاف ولم يخالفه أحد فيما علمت وكيف يخالف وقد نقلوا إجماعهم على الأصل المذكور؟
His statement: (And it is not divided, even if he makes it waqf on his children) meaning the waqf is not divided among its beneficiaries, even if they are the children of the waqf-founder, because they have no right to the corpus, only to the income. And in Fath al-Qadir: They are unanimous that if the whole is waqf on the masters and they want to divide, it is not permissible to apportion. Based on that is the branch that if he makes his house waqf for the dwelling of specific people or his children and his descendants forever, and when they become extinct its income is for the poor, this waqf is valid on this condition, and when they become extinct it is rented and its income is placed for the poor, and none of those entitled to dwelling may rent it even if it exceeds the need of his dwelling. Yes, he may lend it for free. And if the children of this waqf-founder increase, and his children's children and descendants, and the house becomes tight for them, they only have its dwelling divided among their number. And if they are males and females, even if there are rooms and chambers, males may house their wives with them, and females may house their husbands with them, and if there are no rooms, it is not proper to divide among them, nor does apportionment occur; its dwelling is for those whom the waqf-founder gave it, not for others. From this it is known that if some occupy and the other does not find a place sufficient for him, the other does not require the rent of his share from the occupants; rather, if he likes, he may dwell with him in a spot of that house without a wife or husband if any of them has that, otherwise the constrained one leaves and goes out, or they sit together, each in a spot adjacent to the other. And the mentioned principle in the commentaries is the branch in Awaqf al-Khassaf, and no one opposed it as far as I know, and how could they oppose when they have transmitted their consensus on the mentioned principle?
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn phrase 'ولا يقسم' (and it is not divided). It explains that waqf property is not subject to division among beneficiaries because they have no ownership of the corpus (عين) but only a right to the income (غلة) or usufruct. The commentary cites consensus from Fath al-Qadir that division is not allowed. A key application: if someone makes a house waqf for specific people or their descendants to live in, and after they die out, the income goes to the poor. The beneficiaries cannot rent out the house even if they have extra space; they can only lend it for free. If there are many beneficiaries and the house is small, they share the dwelling equally. The rules for co-residence with spouses are given: if there are separate rooms, each can bring their spouse; if not, they cannot. If some occupy more space, the others do not have a right to demand rent; rather they can move in together or the constrained person must leave. The principle is from al-Khassaf's work on waqfs, and there is consensus on it.

Key Terms
غلة (ghullah): Income or produce from waqf property.
مهايأة (muhāyāʾah): Time-sharing or apportionment of usufruct among co-beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf house is too small for all beneficiaries to live comfortably, what is the ruling?
A) They may rent extra space
B) They divide the house by ownership
C) They share the dwelling proportionally
D) The house is sold and proceeds distributed

Key Takeaway
Waqf corpus is indivisible; beneficiaries hold only rights to usufruct, not ownership of the corpus.

Division of Waqf by Agreement and Liability for Rent in Forcible Use
Rulings on division and forcible use of waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid division of waqf among beneficiaries and apply the ruling that forcible use of waqf by a co-beneficiary requires paying rent for the other's share.

Core Idea
Division of waqf for preservation with consent is valid, but forcible use demands rent for the partner's share.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two distinct yet related waqf issues: whether beneficiaries can divide waqf property among themselves, and what happens if one uses the property by force. The author reconciles apparent contradictions by distinguishing between division of ownership and division of preservation, and clarifies that forcible use triggers a rent obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of division
Distinguish between division for preservation (qismat ḥifẓ wa ʿimārah) and division for ownership. Only the former is permissible with consent.
The text contrasts al-Khassaf's view on ownership division with al-Is'af's on preservation division.
2
State the ruling on forcible use
If one partner in a waqf uses the property by force without permission, he must pay rent for the other's share. This applies whether the waqf is for dwelling or income.
In regular joint ownership (not waqf), no rent is owed even if the whole property is used.
3
Understand the waqf vs joint ownership distinction
The text explicitly notes that in joint ownership (milk mushtarak), a partner using the whole property does not owe rent, but in waqf the same action incurs rent because the waqf's usufruct is shared in a specific manner.
This distinction is crucial for answering fatwa queries.
4
Summarize the reconciliation of conflicting texts
The apparent contradiction between al-Khassaf and al-Is'af is resolved by interpreting al-Khassaf as referring to forced division (ownership) and al-Is'af to consensual preservation division. Similarly, al-Khassaf's statement about rent applies only before forcible use.
Ibn Nujaym and al-Ramli offer two reconciliations: one based on type of division, another on forced vs. consensual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الإسعاف : ولو قسمه الواقف بين أربابه ليزرع كل واحد منهم نصيبه وليكون المزروع له دون شركائه توقف على رضاهم ولو فعل أهل الوقف ذلك فيما بينهم جاز ولمن أبي منهم بعد ذلك إبطاله .اهـ. قيدنا بقسمته بين مستحقيه لأن القسمة ليتميز الوقف عن الملك جائزة كما قدمناه في قوله ولا يتم حتى يقبض ويفرز . وفي القنية : ضيعة موقوفة على الموالي فلهم قسمتها قسمة حفظ وعمارة لا قسمة تملك .اهـ. وفي القنية : أحد الشريكين إذا استعمل الوقف بالغلبة بدون إذن الآخر فعليه أجر حصة الشريك، سواء كانت وقفاً على سكناهما أو موقوفة للاستغلال، وفي الملك المشترك لا يلزم الأجر على الشريك إذا استعمل كله وإن كان معداً للإجارة وليس للشريك الذي لم يستعمل الوقف أن يقول للآخر أنا أستعمله بقدر ما استعملت لأن المهايأة إنما تكون بعد الخصومة .اهـ. فعلى هذا قول الخصاف الآخر أجرة معناه قبل السكنى لو طلب أن يجعل عليه شيئاً، أما بعد السكني يستوجب لا أن يكون ذلك بأمر الحاكم احتياطاً في موضع الخلاف قوله: (لا يستوجب الآخر أجرة) قال الرملي : سيأتي في آخر المقولة تقييده بما إذا لم يسكن بالغلبة، أما إذا سكن بها استوجب أجرة حصته. قوله : (والأصل المذكور قال الرملي يعني أن الموقوف عليهم السكنى ليس لهم إلا السكني اهـ . قلت : والأظهر أنه أراد به ما قدمه من قوله وأجمعوا أن الكل لو كان وقفاً على الأرباب الخ». قوله : (وفي الإسعاف ولو قسمه الواقف الخ قال الرملي : يعني أنه يخالف ما تقدم. وأقول : قد يوفق بين القولين بما في القنية من قوله ضيعة موقوفة على الموالي فلهم قسمتها قسمة حفظ وعمارة لا قسمة تملك فيحمل ما في الخصاف على قسمة التملك، وما في الإسعاف على قسمة الحفظ والعمارة. وقد ذكر في فتاوى الحلبي أن قسمة التناوب فيه جائزة ومثل له بمسألة الأرض المذكورة فهو مؤيد لما قلته تأمل اهـ . قلت : وقد يوفق أيضاً بأن ما في الخصاف محمول على قسمة الجبر وما في الإسعاف على قسمة التراضي بلا لزوم ولذا قال : ولمن أبى منهم بعد ذلك إبطاله. قوله : (فعلى هذا قول الخصاف لا يستوجب الخ قال الرملي : كان يخالج خاطري أن هذا سهو لكني كنت أمسك
And in al-Is'af: If the waqf-founder divides it among its masters so that each one plants his share and the crop becomes his without his partners, it is dependent on their consent. If the people of the waqf do that among themselves, it is permissible, and whoever refuses among them can revoke it thereafter. We restricted it to division among its beneficiaries because division to distinguish waqf from ownership is permissible, as we presented in his statement: 'and it is not completed until it is taken possession of and separated'. And in al-Qunyah: A farm waqf on the masters, they have its division as a division of preservation and maintenance, not a division of ownership. And in al-Qunyah: One of the two partners, if he uses the waqf by force without the permission of the other, then he must pay the rent of the partner's share, whether it is a waqf for their dwelling or a waqf for income. In joint ownership, rent is not obligatory on the partner if he uses it all even if it was prepared for rent, and the partner who did not use the waqf cannot say to the other: I will use it to the extent you used, because apportionment only happens after dispute. According to this, the statement of al-Khassaf 'the other does not require rent' means before dwelling, if he requests to place something on him. As for after dwelling, he is not owed unless that is by order of the judge as a precaution in the place of difference. His statement: (the other does not require rent) said al-Ramli: later in the statement its restriction will come to when he did not dwell by force, but if he dwells there, he owes the rent of his share. His statement: (and the mentioned principle) said al-Ramli: means that those entitled to dwelling have only the dwelling. I say: the most apparent is that he meant by it what he presented of his statement: 'and they unanimously agree that if the whole is waqf on the masters...'. His statement: (and in al-Is'af, if the waqf-founder divides it etc.) said al-Ramli: meaning it contradicts what preceded. And I say: it may be reconciled between the two statements by what is in al-Qunyah from his statement: 'a farm waqf on the masters, they have its division as a division of preservation and maintenance, not a division of ownership'. So what is in al-Khassaf is taken as a division of ownership, and what is in al-Is'af is a division of preservation and maintenance. And it is mentioned in Fatawa al-Halabi that rotating division is permissible in it, and he gave an example with the mentioned land issue, it supports what I said. I say: it may also be reconciled by that what is in al-Khassaf is taken as a forced division, and what is in al-Is'af is a consensual division without binding, therefore he said: whoever refuses among them can revoke it. His statement: (according to this, the statement of al-Khassaf 'the other does not require rent' etc.) said al-Ramli: it occurred to my mind that this is a mistake, but I was holding back...
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage contains several related rulings and commentary. First, from al-Is'af: If the waqf-founder divides the waqf land among the beneficiaries for cultivation, each gets his share's crop, but this requires the consent of all beneficiaries. If the beneficiaries themselves agree to such a division, it is valid but any dissenter can revoke it later. The author (Ibn Nujaym) notes that this is a division for preservation (قسمة حفظ وعمارة) not ownership division, as clarified in al-Qunyah. Then from al-Qunyah: A farm waqf on the masters can be divided for preservation and maintenance, not for ownership. Then another ruling from al-Qunyah: If one of two partners in a waqf uses the property by force without permission, he must pay rent for the other's share. This applies whether the waqf is for dwelling or for income. In regular joint ownership (not waqf), no rent is owed if one partner uses the whole property, even if it was for rent. The partner who does not use cannot demand use in kind; only monetary compensation after dispute. The author then reconciles apparent contradictions: al-Khassaf's statement that 'the other does not require rent' is interpreted as referring to cases without forcible use. Al-Ramli comments on various points, noting that al-Is'af seems to contradict earlier statements but can be reconciled by distinguishing between division of ownership (not allowed) and division of preservation (allowed). He also mentions a ruling from Fatawa al-Halabi about rotating division (قسمة التناوب) being permissible. The passage ends with al-Ramli's doubt about a potential error.

Key Terms
قسمة حفظ وعمارة (qismat ḥifẓ wa ʿimārah): Division of waqf property for preservation and maintenance, not for ownership.
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Using property forcibly without permission.
قسمة التناوب (qismat al-tanāwub): Rotating division of usufruct, where beneficiaries take turns using the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when one beneficiary uses waqf property by force without the other's permission?
A) He owes no rent because it is waqf.
B) He must pay rent for the other's share.
C) He can be evicted by the other beneficiary.
D) The property is no longer valid waqf.

Key Takeaway
Division of waqf for preservation by mutual consent is valid; forcible use obligates rent for the other's share.

Dwelling Rights and Rent Liability in Waqf
Ruling on dwelling shares and rent liability among waqf beneficiaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rent liability for surplus occupation in a waqf dwelling and identify the consensus proof (ijma) cited by al-Khassaf.

Core Idea
In a waqf dwelling, beneficiaries do not owe rent for surplus space unless they seized it by force.

When a waqf is designated for dwelling (sukna) and the number of beneficiaries increases, the space must be shared equally. A natural question arises: if one beneficiary occupies more than his share, must he compensate the others? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, grounded in the works of al-Khassaf and supported by scholarly consensus, and clarifies the exception for forcible seizure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The passage addresses a waqf for dwelling with multiple beneficiaries. The key question is whether a beneficiary who takes more than his share owes rent to the others.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The default ruling is that no rent is due unless the beneficiary occupied the surplus by force (ghalabah). Mere occupation without force does not create rent liability.
This is the mufta bihi position from the zahir al-riwayah.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof is ijma (consensus) as transmitted by al-Khassaf. The text states that no one opposed this principle, and consensus was narrated on it.
The consensus is zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalalah according to Hanafis.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Ramli) conditioned rent liability on force. This refines the ruling without contradicting the original principle.
The ikhtilaf is on the condition, not the default.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a waqf house with three beneficiaries, one occupies an extra room without force. He does not owe rent; the others may request to join him in his room or seek other arrangements.
If he locked the door and prevented entry, that would be force and rent would be due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على قدر حاجة سكناه نعم له الإعارة لا غير. ولو كثر أولاد هذا الواقف وولد ولده ونسله ضاقت الدار عليهم ليس لهم إلا سكناها تقسط على عددهم. ولو كانوا ذكوراً وإناثاً، حتى إن كان فيها حجر ومقاصير كان للذكور أن يسكنوا نساءهم معهم وللنساء أن يسكن أزواجهن معهن، وإن لم يكن فيها حجر لا يستقيم أن تقسم بينهم ولا يقع فيها مهايأة إنما سكناها لمن جعل الواقف له ذلك لا لغيرهم. وعن هذا يعرف أنه لو سكن بعضهم فلم يجد الآخر موضعاً يكفيه لا يستوجب الآخر أجرة حصته على الساكنين بل إن أحب أن يسكن معه في بقعة من تلك الدار بلا زوجة أو زوج إن كان لأحدهم ذلك وإلا ترك المتضيق وخرج أو جلسوا معاً كل في بقعة إلى جنب الآخر. والأصل المذكور في الشروح الفرع في أوقاف الخصاف ولم يخالفه أحد فيما علمت وكيف يخالف وقد نقلوا إجماعهم على الأصل المذكور؟
In proportion to the need of his dwelling, yes he may lend (to others) and nothing else. If the children of this waqif become many, and his children's children and his descendants, and the house is too narrow for them, they have only the right to inhabit it, divided according to their number, whether they are males or females. If there are rooms and compartments, males may dwell with their wives, and females may dwell with their husbands. If there are no rooms, it is not proper to divide it among them, nor can there be a timed distribution (muhaya'ah); rather, its dwelling is for those for whom the waqif designated it, not others. From this it is known that if some of them dwell (in it) and another does not find sufficient space, the other does not deserve the rent of his share from the dwellers. Rather, if he wishes to dwell with him in a part of that house without a wife or husband if any of them has that, otherwise the constricted one leaves and goes out, or they sit together, each in a spot next to the other. The aforementioned principle in the commentaries, the branch in the waqfs of al-Khassaf, no one has opposed it as far as I know, and how could they oppose when they have narrated their consensus on the aforementioned principle?
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for multiple beneficiaries of a waqf designated for dwelling (sukna). The rule is that the beneficiaries have only the right to inhabit as per the waqif's stipulation. If the dwelling becomes insufficient for their numbers, they share it equally by count. If there are separate rooms, male beneficiaries may include their wives, and female beneficiaries may include their husbands. If there are no separate rooms, physical division (qismah) is not possible, nor is a timed rotation (muhaya'ah). The passage then deduces that if one beneficiary occupies more than his share, he does not owe rent to the others for the surplus, unless he seized by force. The text confirms this ruling is from the work of al-Khassaf on waqf, and that there is consensus on this principle.

Key Terms
سكنى (sukna): Right to inhabit (dwelling) in a waqf
مهايأة (muhaya'ah): Timed sharing or rotation of use among beneficiaries
إعارة (i'tarah): Gratuitous loan (to allow another to use the space)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if a beneficiary occupies surplus space in a waqf dwelling without using force?
A) He must pay rent proportional to the surplus.
B) He does not owe rent; the constricted beneficiary may join him or leave.
C) He must vacate immediately.
D) The waqf is dissolved.

Key Takeaway
In a waqf dwelling, beneficiaries share the right to inhabit; no rent is due for surplus use unless the surplus was obtained by force.

Resolving the Dispute on Dividing Waqf Land Among Beneficiaries
Resolving differing opinions on division of waqf land for farming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of al-Khassaf and al-Is'af on division of waqf land and explain the Hanafi reconciliation using the distinction between division of ownership and division for maintenance.

Core Idea
Division for use is valid; division for ownership is not.

The Hanafi school presents a seeming conflict on dividing waqf land: al-Khassaf prohibits any division, while al-Is'af allows it. Commentators reconcile by distinguishing division that transfers ownership (invalid) from division that preserves the property (valid with consent). This lesson walks through the dispute and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting rulings
Al-Khassaf prohibits division; al-Is'af allows it with consent and allows revocation.
2
Understand the first reconciliation
The commentator invokes al-Qunyah's distinction: division for preservation and maintenance is permissible; division for ownership is not.
3
Apply the distinction
Al-Khassaf's prohibition refers to division of ownership; al-Is'af refers to division for use.
4
Examine the second reconciliation
Another reconciliation: al-Khassaf refers to compulsory division; al-Is'af to voluntary division which can be revoked.
5
Determine the practical outcome
Beneficiaries may voluntarily divide for use; the division is not binding; any party can revoke. If one uses by force, rent is owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الإسعاف : ولو قسمه الواقف بين أربابه ليزرع كل واحد منهم نصيبه وليكون اهـ. المزروع له دون شركائه توقف على رضاهم ولو فعل أهل الوقف ذلك فيما بينهم جاز ولمن أبي منهم بعد ذلك إبطاله .اهـ. قيدنا بقسمته بين مستحقيه لأن القسمة ليتميز الوقف عن الملك جائزة كما قدمناه في قوله ولا يتم حتى يقبض ويفرز . وفي القنية : ضيعة موقوفة على الموالي فلهم قسمتها قسمة حفظ وعمارة لا قسمة تملك .اهـ. وفي القنية : أحد الشريكين إذا استعمل الوقف بالغلبة بدون إذن الآخر فعليه أجر حصة الشريك، سواء كانت وقفاً على سكناهما أو موقوفة للاستغلال، وفي الملك المشترك لا يلزم الأجر على الشريك إذا استعمل كله وإن كان معداً للإجارة وليس للشريك الذي لم يستعمل الوقف أن يقول للآخر أنا أستعمله بقدر ما استعملت لأن المهايأة إنما تكون بعد الخصومة .اهـ. فعلى هذا قول الخصاف الآخر أجرة معناه قبل السكنى لو طلب أن يجعل عليه شيئاً، أما بعد السكني يستوجب لا أن يكون ذلك بأمر الحاكم احتياطاً في موضع الخلاف قوله: (لا يستوجب الآخر أجرة) قال الرملي : سيأتي في آخر المقولة تقييده بما إذا لم يسكن بالغلبة، أما إذا سكن بها استوجب أجرة حصته. قوله : (والأصل المذكور قال الرملي يعني أن الموقوف عليهم السكنى ليس لهم إلا السكني اهـ . قلت : والأظهر أنه أراد به ما قدمه من قوله وأجمعوا أن الكل لو كان وقفاً على الأرباب الخ». قوله : (وفي الإسعاف ولو قسمه الواقف الخ قال الرملي : يعني أنه يخالف ما تقدم. وأقول : قد يوفق بين القولين بما في القنية من قوله ضيعة موقوفة على الموالي فلهم قسمتها قسمة حفظ وعمارة لا قسمة تملك فيحمل ما في الخصاف على قسمة التملك، وما في الإسعاف على قسمة الحفظ والعمارة. وقد ذكر في فتاوى الحلبي أن قسمة التناوب فيه جائزة ومثل له بمسألة الأرض المذكورة فهو مؤيد لما قلته تأمل اهـ . قلت : وقد يوفق أيضاً بأن ما في الخصاف محمول على قسمة الجبر وما في الإسعاف على قسمة التراضي بلا لزوم ولذا قال : ولمن أبى منهم بعد ذلك إبطاله. قوله : (فعلى هذا قول الخصاف لا يستوجب الخ قال الرملي : كان يخالج خاطري أن هذا سهو لكني كنت أمسك نفسي عن الكتابة عليه حتى طلبت من بعض الإخوان نسخة النهر من هذا المكان فرأيته قال : وعندي لاختلاف الموضوع، وذلك أن ما في القنية فيما إذا استعمله بالغلبة وما في الخصاف أن هذا سهو
In al-Is'af: If the waqif divides it among its owners so that each of them plants his share and the... the crop is for him without his partners, it is contingent on their consent. If the people of the waqf do that among themselves, it is permissible, and it is permissible for anyone who refuses to annul it afterwards. We restrict this to his division among its entitled parties because division making the waqf distinct from ownership is permissible as we presented in his statement 'it is not complete until receipt and segregation'. In al-Qunyah: A farm waqf on the mawali (clients), they may divide it as a division of preservation and maintenance, not a division of ownership. In al-Qunyah: One of two partners if he uses the waqf by force without permission of the other, he owes the rent of the partner's share, whether it is a waqf for their dwelling or a waqf for exploitation. In common ownership (joint property), the partner is not obliged to pay rent if he uses all of it, even if it is prepared for rent. The partner who did not use the waqf cannot say to the other 'I will use it to the extent you used' because the timed rotation (muhaya'ah) only comes after litigation. On this basis, the other statement of al-Khassaf about rent means before dwelling if he asks to impose something on him; but after dwelling, he does not deserve rent unless it is by order of the judge as a precaution in a point of disagreement. His statement: 'The other does not deserve rent' – al-Ramli said: Restriction will come at the end of the discourse to when he did not dwell by force; if he dwelt by force, he deserves the rent of his share. His statement: 'The aforementioned principle' – al-Ramli said: meaning that those entitled to dwelling have only dwelling. I say: The most apparent is that he intended what he presented earlier from his statement 'and they agreed that if all are owners of the waqf...'. His statement: 'In al-Is'af, if the waqif divides it' – al-Ramli said: meaning that it contradicts what came before. I say: A reconciliation between the two may be achieved by what is in al-Qunyah from his statement: 'A farm waqf on the mawali, they may divide it as a division of preservation and maintenance, not a division of ownership'. So what is in al-Khassaf is carried on division of ownership, and what is in al-Is'af on division of preservation and maintenance. It is mentioned in Fatawa al-Halabi that division by rotation is permissible, and he gave the example of the aforementioned land issue, which supports what I said. I say: It may also be reconciled by that what is in al-Khassaf is carried on compulsory division (qismat al-jabr) and what is in al-Is'af on voluntary division (qismat al-taradi) without bindingness, and therefore he said: 'and it is permissible for anyone who refuses to annul it afterwards'. His statement: 'On this basis, the statement of al-Khassaf that the other does not deserve rent' – al-Ramli said: It occurred to my mind that this is an oversight, but I refrained from writing about it until I asked some brothers for a copy of al-Nahr from this place, and I saw that he said: 'In my view, due to difference of subject, that what is in al-Qunyah is when he used it by force, and what is in al-Khassaf that this is an oversight'.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of dividing waqf property among its beneficiaries. It quotes from al-Is'af that if the waqif himself divides the land among beneficiaries for farming, it depends on their consent. If they agree, it is valid, and any dissenter can later revoke it. This is contrasted with the ruling from al-Khassaf that appears to prohibit division. The commentator reconciles the two by noting that al-Khassaf's prohibition refers to division of ownership (qismat tamalluk), which is not allowed, while al-Is'af's allowance refers to division for preservation and maintenance (qismat hifz wa 'imarah). Another reconciliation is that al-Khassaf speaks of compulsory division (qismat al-jabr) while al-Is'af speaks of voluntary division (qismat al-taradi) which is not binding. The passage also includes a discussion of rent liability when one beneficiary uses the waqf by force, connecting it to the earlier ruling.

Key Terms
قسمة حفظ وعمارة (qismat hifz wa 'imarah): Division for purposes of preservation and maintenance
قسمة تملك (qismat tamalluk): Division that transfers ownership
قسمة الجبر (qismat al-jabr): Compulsory division by a judge
قسمة التراضي (qismat al-taradi): Voluntary division with mutual consent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of division of waqf property is permissible among beneficiaries according to the reconciliation in the text?
A) Division of ownership.
B) Division of use and maintenance.
C) Division by force.
D) Division that changes ownership.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits division of waqf property among beneficiaries for purposes of preservation and maintenance with mutual consent, but not division that transfers ownership.

Priority of Maintenance over Other Expenditure from Waqf Revenue
Ruling that waqf revenue must be spent on maintenance first

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that waqf revenue must first be spent on necessary maintenance and apply the maxim 'al-kharaj bi al-daman' to justify this priority.

Core Idea
Waqf revenue must first preserve the property; maintenance is an implied condition of the endowment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq outlines the Hanafi ruling that the revenue (ghallah) of a waqf property must first be used for its maintenance ('imarah) before any other expenditure. The authors provide a legal proof based on the waqif's implicit intent and the principle that liability accompanies profit. We explore when improvements require beneficiary consent and how to balance maintenance with other charitable spending.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is spending waqf revenue. The ruling is that maintenance is obligatory (wajib) and takes priority over other uses.
The text begins by stating 'يبدأ من غلته بعمارته' (he begins from its revenue with its maintenance).
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are given: (a) The waqif's intent of perpetuity implies maintenance; (b) The maxim 'al-kharaj bi al-daman' analogized to a bequest of a slave's services.
The first dalil is based on 'شرط العمارة اقتضاء' (implied condition); the second on 'ولأن الخراج بالضمان'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The maxim 'liability accompanies profit' means the one receiving the profit (beneficiary) must bear expenses; thus maintenance is on the revenue.
The text explicitly compares to maintenance of a slave whose services are bequeathed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement on improvements beyond the original state: some allow without consent, the preferred view requires consent.
The text says 'والأول أصح' (the first is more correct) requiring consent.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
When damage is caused by a third party, they are liable; maintenance can be delayed if no immediate harm; otherwise, it takes priority.
Quotes from al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Khaniyyah illustrate these scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيؤخذ من الغلة فالأجرة واجبة عليه. وأفاد المصنف من عدم جواز القسمة أن أرض الوقف لو كانت بين اثنين فاقتسماها فلأحدهما إبطالها وأنه لو أجر أحدهما حصته فالأجر بينهما وقيل للمؤجر . والمسألتان في القنية قوله : (ويبدأ من غلته بعمارته بلا (شرط لأن قصد الواقف صرف الغلة مؤبداً ولا تبقى دائماً إلا بالعمارة فثبت شرط العمارة اقتضاء، ولأن الخراج بالضمان وصار كنفقة العبد الموصي بخدمته فإنها على الموصى له بها، ثم إن كان الوقف على الفقراء لا يؤخذون به لعدم تعينهم وأقرب أموالهم هذه الغلة فتجب العمارة فيها، ولو كان الوقف على رجل بعينه وآخره للفقراء فهي في ماله أي مال شاء إذا كان حياً ولا لأنه معين يمكن مطالبته وإنما تستحق العمارة عليه بقدر ما يبقى الموقوف على الصفة التي وقفه، فإن خرب يبني على ذلك الوصف لأنها بصفتها صارت غلتها مصروفة إلى الموقوف عليه، فأما الزيادة على ذلك فليست بمستحقة والغلة مستحقة له فلا يجوز صرفه إلى شيء آخر إلا برضاه، ولو كان الوقف على الفقراء فكذلك عند البعض وعند الآخرين يجوز ذلك والأول أصح لأن الصرف إلى العمارة ضرورة إبقاء مقصود الواقف ولا ضرورة في الزيادة؛ كذا في الهداية. وبهذا علم أن عمارة الأوقاف زيادة على ما كانت العين عليه زمن الواقف لا يجوز إلا برضا المستحقين وظاهر قوله بقدر ما يبقى الموقوف على الصفة منع البياض والحمرة على الحيطان من مال الوقف إن لم يكن فعله الواقف وإن فعله فلا منع . ثم اعلم أن التعمير إنما يكون من غلة الوقف إذا لم يكن الخراب بصنع أحد ولذا قال في الولوالجية : رجل أجر داراً موقوفة فجعل المستأجر رواقها مربطاً يربط فيه الدواب وخربها يضمن لأنه فعل بغير الإذن اهـ. ومما اتفق عليه أصحاب الفتاوى مربطاً أن القيم إذا استأجر أجبراً للعمارة بدرهم ودانق وأجر مثله فاستعمله درهم في العمارة ونقد الأجرة من مال الوقف يضمن جميع ما نقد لأن الإجارة وقعت له لا للوقف اهـ. وصرحوا في نقش المسجد بالجص وماء الذهب أن المتولي لو فعله من مال الوقف ضمن وقدمناه. وههنا مسائل مهمة في العمارة : الأولى قال في فتح القدير : ولا تؤخر العمارة إذا احتيج إليها . وفي الخانية : إذا اجتمع من غلة الأرض في يد القيم فظهر له وجه من وجوه البر والوقف محتاج إلى الإصلاح والعمارة أيضاً ويخاف القيم أنه لو صرف الغلة إلى العمارة يفوت ذلك البر فإنه ينظر؛ إنه إن لم يكن في تأخير إصلاح الأرض ومرمته إلى الغلة الثانية ضرر بين يخاف خراب الوقف فإنه يصرف الغلة إلى ذلك البر وتؤخر المرمة إلى الغلة الثانية، وإن كان في تأخير المرمة ضرر بين فإنه يصرف الغلة إلى المرمة فإن فضل شيء يصرف إلى ذلك البر
So it is taken from the revenue, so the rent is obligatory upon him. And the author deduced from the impermissibility of division that if waqf land were between two persons and they divided it, each of them can revoke it, and that if one of them rents his share, the rent is between them, and it is said for the lessor. Both issues are in al-Qunyah. His statement: (And he begins from its revenue with its maintenance without a condition) because the intention of the waqif is to spend the revenue perpetually, and it cannot remain permanent except by maintenance, so the condition of maintenance is established implicitly; and because liability accompanies profit, and it becomes like the maintenance of a slave whose services are bequeathed, for it is upon the one to whom the bequest is made. Then, if the waqf is for the poor, they cannot be bound by it because they are not specific, and the nearest of their properties is this revenue, so maintenance is obligatory upon it. If the waqf is for a specific man and its end is for the poor, then it is upon his property, whichever property he wishes, as long as he is alive; because he is a specific person who can be called upon. Maintenance is only due upon him to the extent that the waqf remains in the condition in which it was endowed. If it falls into ruin, he rebuilds it according to that description, because its revenue was spent on the beneficiary. As for beyond that, it is not entitled, and the revenue is entitled to him, so it is not permissible to spend it on anything else except with his consent. If the waqf is for the poor, it is likewise according to some, and according to others it is permissible, and the first is more correct because spending on maintenance is a necessity to preserve the intention of the waqif, and there is no necessity in increase. This is from al-Hidayah. From this it is known that maintenance of waqf beyond what the property was upon at the time of the waqif is not permissible except with the consent of the beneficiaries, and the apparent meaning of his statement 'to the extent that the waqf remains in the condition' prohibits whitewashing and red coloring on walls from waqf money if the waqif did not do it; if he did it, there is no prohibition. Then know that maintenance is only from the revenue of the waqf if the ruin was not by the action of anyone. Therefore, it is said in al-Walwaljiyyah: A man rented a waqf house and the lessee made its portico a stable, tying animals there, and ruined it; he is liable because he did it without permission. And from what the fatwa-givers agreed upon: If the superintendent (qayyim) hired labourers for maintenance for one dirham and a daniq, and the rental equivalent was used, and he spent a dirham on maintenance and paid the wage from waqf money, he is liable for all he paid because the hire contract was for him, not for the waqf. And they explicitly stated in the case of decorating the mosque with plaster and gold leaf that if the caretaker did it from waqf money, he is liable, and we have presented it. And here are important issues regarding maintenance: First, it is said in Fath al-Qadir: Maintenance is not delayed when needed. And in al-Khaniyyah: If revenue from land in the hands of the superintendent accumulates, and he sees a charitable purpose, and the waqf also needs repair and maintenance, and the superintendent fears that if he spends the revenue on maintenance, the charity will be missed, then he considers: If delaying repair and maintenance until the next season does not cause clear damage that threatens ruin of the waqf, then he spends the revenue on the charity and delays maintenance until the next season. If delaying maintenance causes clear damage, then he spends the revenue on maintenance, and if anything remains, he spends it on that (charity).
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage discusses the priority of spending waqf revenue on maintenance (al-'imarah). The ruling is that the waqf's revenue must first be used to maintain the property, because the waqif's intent is to perpetually benefit from the property, and perpetual benefit depends on maintenance. This is an implied condition of the waqf. Additionally, the principle 'al-kharaj bi al-daman' (liability accompanies profit) applies. The passage then distinguishes between necessary maintenance and improvements beyond the original state. Necessary maintenance is obligatory; improvements require the consent of the beneficiaries. Quoting from al-Hidayah, the text states that spending on maintenance is a necessity to preserve the waqif's purpose, while improvements are not. The passage also notes that maintenance costs are taken from revenue only if the damage was not caused by someone's fault. If caused by a third party, that party is liable. Then it provides rules for the superintendent (qayyim) regarding hiring workers and the liability for wrong payments. Finally, it addresses a scenario where revenue could be spent on charitable causes but maintenance is needed: if delaying maintenance does not cause immediate harm, the revenue may be spent on charity; otherwise, maintenance takes priority.

Key Terms
عمارة ('imarah): Maintenance and repair of waqf property to keep it functional
غلة (ghallah): Revenue or produce of the waqf property (e.g., rent, crops)
خراج بالضمان (kharaj bi al-daman): Legal maxim: 'Liability accompanies profit'; one who enjoys the profit must bear the expenses/losses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the supervisor of a waqf delay maintenance and spend the revenue on other charitable purposes?
A) Always delay maintenance.
B) Only if the waqf is for specific individuals.
C) If delaying maintenance does not cause immediate damage to the property.
D) Never, maintenance must always be done first.

Key Takeaway
Maintenance of waqf property from its revenue is obligatory (wajib) and takes priority over all other expenditures, based on the waqif's implied condition and the maxim 'al-kharaj bi al-daman'.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
10 min
The Obligation of Waqf Maintenance: Proofs and Priority
Commentary establishing the obligatory priority of maintenance over distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that maintenance of waqf property is wajib and explain the qiyas proof based on the slave analogy.

Core Idea
Waqf revenue must first cover maintenance because the endower's intent is perpetuity—preservation precedes distribution.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the commentator expands on the matn's statement that maintenance is taken from waqf revenue without any explicit condition. He provides two proofs: the endower's implicit condition of perpetuity, and the analogy to a bequeathed slave. Understanding this priority is essential for anyone managing a waqf (mutawalli).

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The text states that maintenance (عمارة) is taken from the waqf revenue (غلة) without any condition imposed by the endower. This is the starting point.
The ruling is wajib, not just recommended.
2
Understand the first proof: implied condition
The endower intends perpetual charity; the waqf cannot endure without maintenance, so maintenance is impliedly required by the endower's purpose.
This is an application of the principle of maqasid (purposes).
3
Analyze the second proof: al-kharaj bi al-daman and qiyas
The maxim 'profit is in return for liability' (الخراج بالضمان) indicates that the one who enjoys the benefit must bear the costs. This is analogized to a bequeathed slave: the legatee must maintain the slave because he benefits from his services. Similarly, waqf beneficiaries benefit from the revenue, so they must bear maintenance, but since the poor are unspecified, maintenance is taken from the revenue itself.
The illa (effective cause) is enjoyment of benefit (الانتفاع بالمنفعة).
4
Distinguish between types of beneficiaries
If the waqf is for specific individuals, maintenance is on them individually (to the extent needed). If for the poor in general, maintenance is obligatory from the revenue because they are not individually liable.
This affects who bears the immediate cost.

ويبدأ من غلته بعمارته بلا شرط لأن قصد الواقف صرف الغلة مؤبداً ولا تبقى دائماً إلا بالعمارة فثبت شرط العمارة اقتضاء، ولأن الخراج بالضمان وصار كنفقة العبد الموصي بخدمته فإنها على الموصى له بها، ثم إن كان الوقف على الفقراء لا يؤخذون به لعدم تعينهم وأقرب أموالهم هذه الغلة فتجب العمارة فيها، ولو كان الوقف على رجل بعينه وآخره للفقراء فهي في ماله أي مال شاء إذا كان حياً ولا لأنه معين يمكن مطالبته وإنما فلا منع . ثم اعلم أن التعمير إنما يكون من غلة الوقف إذا لم يكن الخراب بصنع أحد ولذا قال في الولوالجية : رجل أجر داراً موقوفة فجعل المستأجر رواقها مربطاً يربط فيه الدواب وخربها يضمن لأنه فعل بغير الإذن وصرحوا في نقش المسجد بالجص وماء الذهب أن المتولي لو فعله من مال الوقف ضمن وقدمناه. وههنا مسائل مهمة في العمارة : الأولى قال في فتح القدير : ولا تؤخر العمارة إذا احتيج إليها . وفي الخانية : إذا اجتمع إلى الغلة الثانية ضرر بين يخاف خراب الوقف فإنه يصرف الغلة إلى ذلك البر وتؤخر المرمة إلى الغلة الثانية، وإن كان في تأخير المرمة ضرر بين فإنه يصرف الغلة إلى المرمة فإن فضل شيء يصرف إلى ذلك البر. والمراد بأهل للتمليك لا يجوز صرف لغلة إليه لأن التصدق عبارة عن التمليك فلا يصح إلا ممن هو من أهل التمليك اهـ. وظاهر أنه يجوز الصرف على المستحقين وتأخير العمارة إلى الغلة الثانية إذا لم يخف ضرر بين الثانية لو الخراج وما يحتاج إليه الوقف من العمارة والمؤنة مستثنى عن حق الفقراء فإذا دفع إليهم ذلك ضمن اهـ. وإذا ضمن ينبغي أن لا يرجع على المستحقين بما دفعه إليهم في هذه الحالة قياساً على مودع الابن إذا أنفق على الأبوين بغير إذنه وبغير إذن القاضي فإنهم قالوا يضمن ولا رجوع له على الأبوين قالوا : لأنه ملكه بالضمان فتبين أنه دفع مال نفسه وأنه متبرع ولا رجوع فيه؛ ذكروه في آخر ماله النفقات. وعلى هذا فينبغي أنه إذا صرف على المستحقين وهناك تعمير واجب فعمر من أن لا يكون متبرعاً بالتعمير ويكون عوضاً عما لزمه بالضمان الثالثة في قطع معاليم المستحقين لأجل العمارة. قال في فتح القدير : وتقطع الجهات الموقوف عليها للعمارة إن لم فيما إذا لم يجد الآخر موضعاً يكفيه فتدبره اهـ. قوله : (وإذا ضمن ينبغي أن لا يرجع على المستحقين الخ) قال الرملي قال في النهر أقول : فيه نظر بل ما دام المدفوع قائماً في يده له الرجوع فيه لا ما إذا هلك إذ قصارى الأمر أنه هبة وفيها له الرجوع ما دامت العين قائمة بالتراضي أو بقضاء القاضي إلا لمانع فتدبره اهـ. أقول : لا وجه لجعله هبة بل هو دفع مال يستحقه غير المدفوع إليه على ظن أنه يستحقه المدفوع إليه فينبغي الرجوع قائماً أو مستهلكاً ويفرق بينه وبين نفقة مودع الابن على الأبوين بأنه مأمور بالحفظ وإنفاقه عليهما ضده إذ هو إتلاف بخلاف الدفع للمستحقين فإنه من جملة ما هو داخل تحت تصرف المتولي في الجملة والمودع لا تصرف له في الوديعة بوجه من الوجوه، فإذا ضمن ملك المدفوع منه لهما على جهة الإنفاق بخلاف المدفوع على جهة أنه حقه فإنه إذا استهلكه على هذا الوجه ولم يكن حقيقة ضمنه كالدين المظنون ملخصه أن مودع الابن دفع للإنفاق ولم يؤمر به فضمن ولا يرجع لإذنه له بها والناظر دفع على أنه استحقاقه وهو آخذه على ذلك هذا، وقد ذكر في جامع الفصولين في الثالث والثلاثين في بيان الغصب : أودعه ثياباً فجعل المودع ثوبه فيها ثم طلب الوديعة ربها فدفع الكل إليه فرب الوديعة يضمن ثوب المودع إذ من أخذ شيئاً على أنه له ولم يكن له ضمنه اهـ. ومقتضى ما ذكر أنه يضمنه المستحق هالكاً أيضاً لأنه أخذه على أنه له وليس له فيضمنه اللهم إلا أن يقال : إنه دفع الثوب ناسياً له فلم يعتبر دفعه له فكأنه أخذه بنفسه من غير دفعه له فكان متعدياً في أخذه لذلك فكانت أمانة في يده تأمل اهـ. وفي شرح المقدسي ما يوافقه حيث قال : وينبغي أن
And he begins from its revenue with its maintenance without condition, because the intention of the endower is to perpetually spend the revenue, and it does not remain perpetual except through maintenance, so the condition of maintenance is established impliedly. And because profit is in return for liability (al-kharaj bi al-daman), and it becomes like the maintenance of a slave whose services are bequeathed, which is incumbent upon the legatee. Then if the waqf is for the poor, they are not held responsible due to their non-specificity, and the closest of their assets is this revenue, so maintenance becomes obligatory therein. If the waqf is for a specific person and ultimately for the poor, then it is from his wealth, i.e., whichever wealth he wishes as long as he is alive? No, because he is specific and can be held accountable; maintenance is only due upon him to the extent that preserves the waqf property in the condition in which it was endowed. So if it deteriorates, he rebuilds it to that description, because by its description, its revenue becomes spent on the waqf beneficiary. As for additional expenditure beyond that, it is not due, and the revenue is due to him, so it is not permissible to spend it on anything else except with his consent. If the waqf is for the poor, then similarly according to some, and according to others it is permissible, and the first is more correct because spending on maintenance is a necessity for preserving the endower's purpose, and there is no necessity for increase; thus in al-Hidaya. And from this it is known that maintenance of waqfs beyond what the property was upon in the time of the endower is not permissible except with the consent of the beneficiaries. And the apparent meaning of his statement 'to the extent that preserves the waqf in its condition' forbids whitewash and red paint on walls from waqf funds if the endower did not do so; if he did, then there is no prohibition. Then know that improvement is only from the waqf revenue if the deterioration was not caused by anyone. Hence it is stated in al-Walwalijiyya: A man leased a house that was a waqf, and the lessee made its porch a stable for tying animals and damaged it; he guarantees it because he acted without permission. And among what the authors of fatwas agreed upon is that if the administrator hired laborers for maintenance for a dirham and a daniq and the like, and he used a dirham for maintenance and paid the wages from waqf funds, he guarantees all that he paid because the hire was for him, not for the waqf. And they explicitly stated regarding the decoration of a mosque with plaster and gold that if the trustee did it from waqf funds, he guarantees, and we have mentioned it earlier. And here are important issues regarding maintenance: The first: It is stated in Fath al-Qadir: Maintenance is not delayed when needed. And in al-Khaniyya: If revenue from land accumulates in the hands of the administrator, and a charitable cause appears to him, and the waqf is also in need of repair and maintenance, and the administrator fears that if he spends the revenue on maintenance, that charitable cause will be missed, then he considers: if there is no obvious harm in delaying the repair and maintenance until the next revenue such that destruction of the waqf is feared, then he spends the revenue on that charitable cause and delays maintenance until the next revenue. But if there is obvious harm in delaying maintenance, then he spends the revenue on maintenance, and if anything remains, he spends it on that charitable cause. What is meant by charitable cause here is a cause where the revenue is given in charity to a type of poor person, such as ransoming Muslim captives or assisting a stranded fighter, because these are deserving of charity. As for building a mosque or a ribat or the like, which are not eligible for ownership, it is not permissible to spend the revenue on them because charity is defined as giving ownership, so it is not valid except to someone eligible for ownership. And it is apparent that it is permissible to spend on the beneficiaries and delay maintenance until the next revenue if no obvious harm is feared. But if the administrator spends on the beneficiaries while there is maintenance that cannot be delayed, then he becomes liable, as in al-Dhakhira: If in that year there was revenue, and the administrator distributed the revenue to the poor and did not retain anything for the land tax (kharaj), then he guarantees the portion of the kharaj, because the amount of the kharaj and what the waqf needs for maintenance and expenses is excluded from the right of the poor. So if he paid that to them, he guarantees it. And if he guarantees, it is appropriate that he not have recourse against the beneficiaries for what he paid to them in this situation, by analogy with the case of a depositor's son who spends on his parents without his permission and without the judge's permission, where they said he guarantees and has no recourse against the parents, because he owns it by virtue of guarantee, so it becomes clear that he paid his own money and was a volunteer, with no recourse. This is mentioned at the end of the chapter on expenditures. And accordingly, it is appropriate that if he spent on the beneficiaries while there was obligatory maintenance, then he is not a volunteer for the maintenance, but it is compensation for what became incumbent upon him due to guarantee. The third issue is about cutting off the stipends of the beneficiaries for the sake of maintenance. It is stated in Fath al-Qadir: The endowments' shares are cut off for maintenance if there is no other sufficient place. Consider it. His statement: 'And if he guarantees, it is appropriate that he not have recourse against the beneficiaries...' Al-Ramli said: In al-Nahr, I say: There is consideration in this. Rather, as long as the payment remains in their hands, he has recourse, not if it perishes, because at most it is a gift, and in a gift he has recourse as long as the object remains, by mutual consent or by a judge's decree, unless there is an impediment. So consider it. I say: There is no basis for calling it a gift; rather it is payment of money that someone else is entitled to, under the assumption that the recipient is entitled to it, so recourse should be possible whether it remains or is consumed. And a distinction is made between this and the spending of the depositor's son on his parents, because the depositor is commanded to preserve, and spending on them is contrary to that, as it is destruction, unlike payment to beneficiaries, which is part of the administrator's authority in general; the depositor has no authority over the deposit whatsoever. So if he guarantees, he owns the money from the recipient on the basis of spending, unlike payment on the basis of right, for if he consumes it in this manner and it was not actually his right, he guarantees it, like a suspected debt. Summary: The depositor's son paid for spending and was not commanded to do so, so he guarantees and does not have recourse because he gave permission? No. The administrator paid on the basis of entitlement, and the recipient took it on that basis. This is mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn in the thirty-third chapter on usurpation: He deposited clothes with him, and the depositary placed his own garment among them, then the owner of the deposit demanded it, and he gave all to him; the owner of the deposit guarantees the depositary's garment because whoever takes something on the basis that it is his when it is not, guarantees it. What is mentioned implies that the beneficiary guarantees it even if it perishes, because he took it on the basis that it is his and it is not, so he guarantees it, unless it is said that he gave the garment forgetting it, so his payment is not considered, so it is as if he took it himself without payment, thus he was a transgressor in taking it, so it remained a trust in his hand. Consider. And in Sharh al-Maqdisi, what supports it is where he said: And it is appropriate that
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, expanding the ruling that maintenance of waqf property is given priority over other expenditures from the waqf's revenue. The author begins by stating the ruling: maintenance (عمارة) is taken from the revenue (غلة) of the waqf without any explicit condition by the endower. This is because the endower's implicit intention is perpetuity, which can only be achieved through maintenance. The proof is based on two lines of reasoning: first, the endower's purpose of perpetual charity requires preservation; second, the legal maxim 'al-kharaj bi al-daman' (profit is in return for liability) — meaning that the one who benefits from the property must bear its burdens. This is then analogized to the case of a slave whose services are bequeathed: the legatee must bear the slave's maintenance because he enjoys the benefit. The commentary then distinguishes between different types of waqf beneficiaries. If the waqf is for the poor in general (non-specific), the maintenance is obligatory from the revenue immediately because the poor are not individually liable. If the waqf is for a specific individual first and then to the poor, the maintenance falls on that individual during his lifetime, but only to the extent necessary to preserve the property in its original condition. Any improvement beyond the original state requires the consent of the beneficiaries. The passage then introduces several important issues (مسائل) regarding maintenance. The first issue: maintenance must not be delayed if needed. However, there is a nuanced ruling from al-Khaniyya: if the administrator has a charitable opportunity (like ransoming captives) and the waqf's maintenance can be safely deferred to the next year's revenue without risk of destruction, it is permissible to spend on charity now and delay maintenance. But if delay would cause obvious harm, maintenance comes first. The second issue concerns the liability of the administrator if he distributes all revenue to beneficiaries while ignoring obligatory maintenance or taxes (خراج). According to al-Dhakhira, the administrator is personally liable for the portion that should have been reserved for maintenance and taxes. A subsequent discussion, citing al-Ramli and others, debates whether the administrator can recover the money from the beneficiaries after being forced to pay from his own pocket. The preferred view is that he can recover it as long as the property remains in the beneficiaries' hands, but if consumed, there is a difference of opinion. The third issue: stipends of beneficiaries may be suspended to fund necessary maintenance. Overall, the passage demonstrates the Hanafi principle that the waqf's preservation takes precedence over current distributions, and that the administrator must balance charitable disbursement with the long-term sustainability of the waqf.

Key Terms
غلة (ghallah): The revenue or produce generated from waqf property, such as rent from real estate or crops from land.
عمارة (imarah): Maintenance and repair of waqf property to keep it in usable condition, including essential repairs but not decorative improvements.
قيم (qayyim): Administrator or custodian of the waqf, also called متولي (mutawalli), responsible for managing the waqf and ensuring its income is properly spent.
الخراج بالضمان (al-kharaj bi al-daman): Legal maxim: 'Profit is in return for liability' — the one who bears the risk of ownership is entitled to the profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof that maintenance of waqf property is wajib from its revenue?
A) The explicit condition of the endower.
B) The implicit condition of the endower's intention of perpetuity.
C) The consensus of the companions.
D) The text of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Maintenance of waqf property is wajib from its revenue, proven by the endower's implied condition and the qiyas on 'al-kharaj bi al-daman'.

Waqf — Endowment
advanced
12 min
Practical Rulings on Waqf Maintenance: Delays, Liability, and Beneficiary Stipends
Commentary detailing practical scenarios for mutawalli balancing maintenance and distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings on delaying maintenance for a charitable cause, determine the mutawalli's liability for improper distribution, and explain when beneficiary stipends can be cut for maintenance.

Core Idea
A mutawalli must balance maintenance and charity, but if distribution without reserving causes harm, he is personally liable.

This lesson covers three important practical issues that a mutawalli faces daily. The first is the permissibility of delaying maintenance when a pressing charitable need arises, provided no harm to the waqf. The second is the liability of the mutawalli if he distributes all revenue without setting aside funds for maintenance and taxes. The third is the authority to suspend beneficiary stipends to fund urgent repairs. These rulings ensure the waqf's sustainability while respecting beneficiaries' rights.

Guided Path
1
Learn the rule on delaying maintenance for a charitable cause
If a charitable opportunity (e.g., ransoming captives) arises and the waqf's maintenance can be safely postponed without risk of destruction, the mutawalli may spend the revenue on charity and delay maintenance to the next year.
The key condition is 'no obvious harm' (لا ضرر بين).
2
Understand the mutawalli's liability for premature distribution
If the mutawalli distributes all revenue to beneficiaries without reserving for necessary maintenance or land tax (kharaj), he personally guarantees the portion that should have been reserved.
This is because that portion is considered excluded from the beneficiaries' right.
3
Analyze the debate on recovery from beneficiaries
There is a difference of opinion whether the mutawalli can recover the money from the beneficiaries after being forced to pay from his own pocket. The preferred view is that he can recover as long as the money remains in their hands, but if consumed, there is no recourse.
This is analogous to a gift but with nuances.
4
Apply the ruling on cutting stipends for maintenance
If the waqf lacks other funds, the stipends (جهات) of the beneficiaries may be temporarily suspended to finance necessary maintenance.
This is from Fath al-Qadir: 'وتقطع الجهات الموقوف عليها للعمارة'.

ويبدأ من غلته بعمارته بلا شرط لأن قصد الواقف صرف الغلة مؤبداً ولا تبقى دائماً إلا بالعمارة فثبت شرط العمارة اقتضاء، ولأن الخراج بالضمان وصار كنفقة العبد الموصي بخدمته فإنها على الموصى له بها، ثم إن كان الوقف على الفقراء لا يؤخذون به لعدم تعينهم وأقرب أموالهم هذه الغلة فتجب العمارة فيها، ولو كان الوقف على رجل بعينه وآخره للفقراء فهي في ماله أي مال شاء إذا كان حياً ولا لأنه معين يمكن مطالبته وإنما تستحق العمارة عليه بقدر ما يبقى الموقوف على الصفة التي وقفه، فإن خرب يبني على ذلك الوصف لأنها بصفتها صارت غلتها مصروفة إلى الموقوف عليه، فأما الزيادة على ذلك فليست بمستحقة والغلة مستحقة له فلا يجوز
