عمارة الأوقاف زيادة على ما كانت العين عليه زمن الواقف لا يجوز إلا برضا المستحقين وظاهر قوله بقدر ما يبقى الموقوف على الصفة منع البياض والحمرة على الحيطان من مال الوقف إن لم يكن فعله الواقف وإن فعله فلا منع . ثم اعلم أن التعمير إنما يكون من غلة الوقف إذا لم يكن الخراب بصنع أحد ولذا قال في الولوالجية : رجل أجر داراً موقوفة فجعل المستأجر رواقها مربطاً يربط فيه الدواب وخربها يضمن لأنه فعل بغير الإذن اهـ. ومما اتفق عليه أصحاب الفتاوى مربطاً أن القيم إذا استأجر أجبراً للعمارة بدرهم ودانق وأجر مثله فاستعمله درهم في العمارة ونقد الأجرة من مال الوقف يضمن جميع ما نقد لأن الإجارة وقعت له لا للوقف اهـ. وصرحوا في نقش المسجد بالجص وماء الذهب أن المتولي لو فعله من مال الوقف ضمن وقدمناه. وههنا مسائل مهمة في العمارة : الأولى قال في فتح القدير : ولا تؤخر العمارة إذا احتيج إليها . وفي الخانية : إذا اجتمع من غلة الأرض في يد القيم فظهر له وجه من وجوه البر والوقف محتاج إلى الإصلاح والعمارة أيضاً ويخاف القيم أنه لو صرف الغلة إلى العمارة يفوت ذلك البر فإنه ينظر؛ إنه إن لم يكن في تأخير إصلاح الأرض ومرمته إلى الغلة الثانية ضرر بين يخاف خراب الوقف فإنه يصرف الغلة إلى ذلك البر وتؤخر المرمة إلى الغلة الثانية، وإن كان في تأخير المرمة ضرر بين فإنه يصرف الغلة إلى المرمة فإن فضل شيء يصرف إلى ذلك البر. والمراد من وجه البر ههنا وجه فيه تصدق بالغلة على نوع من الفقراء نحو فك أسارى المسلمين أو إعانة الغازي المنقطع لأن هؤلاء من أهل التصدق عليهم فجاز صرف الغلة إليهم، فأما عمارة مسجد أو رباط أو نحو ذلك مما هو ليس بأهل للتمليك لا يجوز صرف لغلة إليه لأن التصدق عبارة عن التمليك فلا يصح إلا ممن هو من أهل التمليك اهـ. وظاهر أنه يجوز الصرف على المستحقين وتأخير العمارة إلى الغلة الثانية إذا لم يخف ضرر بين الثانية لو صرف المتولي على المستحقين وهناك عمارة لا يجوز تأخيرها فإنه يكون ضامناً لما في الذخيرة : إذا كانت في تلك السنة غلة ففرق القيم الغلة على المساكين ولم يمسك للخراج شيئاً فإنه يضمن حصة الخراج لأن بقدر الخراج وما يحتاج إليه الوقف من العمارة والمؤنة مستثنى عن حق الفقراء فإذا دفع إليهم ذلك ضمن اهـ. وإذا ضمن ينبغي أن لا يرجع على المستحقين بما دفعه إليهم في هذه الحالة قياساً على مودع الابن إذا أنفق على الأبوين بغير إذنه وبغير إذن القاضي فإنهم قالوا يضمن ولا رجوع له على الأبوين قالوا : لأنه ملكه بالضمان فتبين أنه دفع مال نفسه وأنه متبرع ولا رجوع فيه؛ ذكروه في آخر ماله النفقات. وعلى هذا فينبغي أنه إذا صرف على المستحقين وهناك تعمير واجب فعمر من أن لا يكون متبرعاً بالتعمير ويكون عوضاً عما لزمه بالضمان الثالثة في قطع معاليم المستحقين لأجل العمارة. قال في فتح القدير : وتقطع الجهات الموقوف عليها للعمارة إن لم فيما إذا لم يجد الآخر موضعاً يكفيه فتدبره اهـ. قوله : (وإذا ضمن ينبغي أن لا يرجع على المستحقين الخ) قال الرملي قال في النهر أقول : فيه نظر بل ما دام المدفوع قائماً في يده له الرجوع فيه لا ما إذا هلك إذ قصارى الأمر أنه هبة وفيها له الرجوع ما دامت العين قائمة بالتراضي أو بقضاء القاضي إلا لمانع فتدبره اهـ. أقول : لا وجه لجعله هبة بل هو دفع مال يستحقه غير المدفوع إليه على ظن أنه يستحقه المدفوع إليه فينبغي الرجوع قائماً أو مستهلكاً ويفرق بينه وبين نفقة مودع الابن على الأبوين بأنه مأمور بالحفظ وإنفاقه عليهما ضده إذ هو إتلاف بخلاف الدفع للمستحقين فإنه من جملة ما هو داخل تحت تصرف المتولي في الجملة والمودع لا تصرف له في الوديعة بوجه من الوجوه، فإذا ضمن ملك المدفوع منه لهما على جهة الإنفاق بخلاف المدفوع على جهة أنه حقه فإنه إذا استهلكه على هذا الوجه ولم يكن حقيقة ضمنه كالدين المظنون ملخصه أن مودع الابن دفع للإنفاق ولم يؤمر به فضمن ولا يرجع لإذنه له بها والناظر دفع على أنه استحقاقه وهو آخذه على ذلك هذا، وقد ذكر في جامع الفصولين في الثالث والثلاثين في بيان الغصب : أودعه ثياباً فجعل المودع ثوبه فيها ثم طلب الوديعة ربها فدفع الكل إليه فرب الوديعة يضمن ثوب المودع إذ من أخذ شيئاً على أنه له ولم يكن له ضمنه اهـ. ومقتضى ما ذكر أنه يضمنه المستحق هالكاً أيضاً لأنه أخذه على أنه له وليس له فيضمنه اللهم إلا أن يقال : إنه دفع الثوب ناسياً له فلم يعتبر دفعه له فكأنه أخذه بنفسه من غير دفعه له فكان متعدياً في أخذه لذلك فكانت أمانة في يده تأمل اهـ. وفي شرح المقدسي ما يوافقه حيث قال : وينبغي أن
And he begins from its revenue with its maintenance without condition, because the intention of the endower is to perpetually spend the revenue, and it does not remain perpetual except through maintenance, so the condition of maintenance is established impliedly. And because profit is in return for liability (al-kharaj bi al-daman), and it becomes like the maintenance of a slave whose services are bequeathed, which is incumbent upon the legatee. Then if the waqf is for the poor, they are not held responsible due to their non-specificity, and the closest of their assets is this revenue, so maintenance becomes obligatory therein. If the waqf is for a specific person and ultimately for the poor, then it is from his wealth, i.e., whichever wealth he wishes as long as he is alive? No, because he is specific and can be held accountable; maintenance is only due upon him to the extent that preserves the waqf property in the condition in which it was endowed. So if it deteriorates, he rebuilds it to that description, because by its description, its revenue becomes spent on the waqf beneficiary. As for additional expenditure beyond that, it is not due, and the revenue is due to him, so it is not permissible to spend it on anything else except with his consent. If the waqf is for the poor, then similarly according to some, and according to others it is permissible, and the first is more correct because spending on maintenance is a necessity for preserving the endower's purpose, and there is no necessity for increase; thus in al-Hidaya. And from this it is known that maintenance of waqfs beyond what the property was upon in the time of the endower is not permissible except with the consent of the beneficiaries. And the apparent meaning of his statement 'to the extent that preserves the waqf in its condition' forbids whitewash and red paint on walls from waqf funds if the endower did not do so; if he did, then there is no prohibition. Then know that improvement is only from the waqf revenue if the deterioration was not caused by anyone. Hence it is stated in al-Walwalijiyya: A man leased a house that was a waqf, and the lessee made its porch a stable for tying animals and damaged it; he guarantees it because he acted without permission. And among what the authors of fatwas agreed upon is that if the administrator hired laborers for maintenance for a dirham and a daniq and the like, and he used a dirham for maintenance and paid the wages from waqf funds, he guarantees all that he paid because the hire was for him, not for the waqf. And they explicitly stated regarding the decoration of a mosque with plaster and gold that if the trustee did it from waqf funds, he guarantees, and we have mentioned it earlier. And here are important issues regarding maintenance: The first: It is stated in Fath al-Qadir: Maintenance is not delayed when needed. And in al-Khaniyya: If revenue from land accumulates in the hands of the administrator, and a charitable cause appears to him, and the waqf is also in need of repair and maintenance, and the administrator fears that if he spends the revenue on maintenance, that charitable cause will be missed, then he considers: if there is no obvious harm in delaying the repair and maintenance until the next revenue such that destruction of the waqf is feared, then he spends the revenue on that charitable cause and delays maintenance until the next revenue. But if there is obvious harm in delaying maintenance, then he spends the revenue on maintenance, and if anything remains, he spends it on that charitable cause. What is meant by charitable cause here is a cause where the revenue is given in charity to a type of poor person, such as ransoming Muslim captives or assisting a stranded fighter, because these are deserving of charity. As for building a mosque or a ribat or the like, which are not eligible for ownership, it is not permissible to spend the revenue on them because charity is defined as giving ownership, so it is not valid except to someone eligible for ownership. And it is apparent that it is permissible to spend on the beneficiaries and delay maintenance until the next revenue if no obvious harm is feared. But if the administrator spends on the beneficiaries while there is maintenance that cannot be delayed, then he becomes liable, as in al-Dhakhira: If in that year there was revenue, and the administrator distributed the revenue to the poor and did not retain anything for the land tax (kharaj), then he guarantees the portion of the kharaj, because the amount of the kharaj and what the waqf needs for maintenance and expenses is excluded from the right of the poor. So if he paid that to them, he guarantees it. And if he guarantees, it is appropriate that he not have recourse against the beneficiaries for what he paid to them in this situation, by analogy with the case of a depositor's son who spends on his parents without his permission and without the judge's permission, where they said he guarantees and has no recourse against the parents, because he owns it by virtue of guarantee, so it becomes clear that he paid his own money and was a volunteer, with no recourse. This is mentioned at the end of the chapter on expenditures. And accordingly, it is appropriate that if he spent on the beneficiaries while there was obligatory maintenance, then he is not a volunteer for the maintenance, but it is compensation for what became incumbent upon him due to guarantee. The third issue is about cutting off the stipends of the beneficiaries for the sake of maintenance. It is stated in Fath al-Qadir: The endowments' shares are cut off for maintenance if there is no other sufficient place. Consider it. His statement: 'And if he guarantees, it is appropriate that he not have recourse against the beneficiaries...' Al-Ramli said: In al-Nahr, I say: There is consideration in this. Rather, as long as the payment remains in their hands, he has recourse, not if it perishes, because at most it is a gift, and in a gift he has recourse as long as the object remains, by mutual consent or by a judge's decree, unless there is an impediment. So consider it. I say: There is no basis for calling it a gift; rather it is payment of money that someone else is entitled to, under the assumption that the recipient is entitled to it, so recourse should be possible whether it remains or is consumed. And a distinction is made between this and the spending of the depositor's son on his parents, because the depositor is commanded to preserve, and spending on them is contrary to that, as it is destruction, unlike payment to beneficiaries, which is part of the administrator's authority in general; the depositor has no authority over the deposit whatsoever. So if he guarantees, he owns the money from the recipient on the basis of spending, unlike payment on the basis of right, for if he consumes it in this manner and it was not actually his right, he guarantees it, like a suspected debt. Summary: The depositor's son paid for spending and was not commanded to do so, so he guarantees and does not have recourse because he gave permission? No. The administrator paid on the basis of entitlement, and the recipient took it on that basis. This is mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn in the thirty-third chapter on usurpation: He deposited clothes with him, and the depositary placed his own garment among them, then the owner of the deposit demanded it, and he gave all to him; the owner of the deposit guarantees the depositary's garment because whoever takes something on the basis that it is his when it is not, guarantees it. What is mentioned implies that the beneficiary guarantees it even if it perishes, because he took it on the basis that it is his and it is not, so he guarantees it, unless it is said that he gave the garment forgetting it, so his payment is not considered, so it is as if he took it himself without payment, thus he was a transgressor in taking it, so it remained a trust in his hand. Consider. And in Sharh al-Maqdisi, what supports it is where he said: And it is appropriate that

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, expanding the ruling that maintenance of waqf property is given priority over other expenditures from the waqf's revenue. The author begins by stating the ruling: maintenance (عمارة) is taken from the revenue (غلة) of the waqf without any explicit condition by the endower. This is because the endower's implicit intention is perpetuity, which can only be achieved through maintenance. The proof is based on two lines of reasoning: first, the endower's purpose of perpetual charity requires preservation; second, the legal maxim 'al-kharaj bi al-daman' (profit is in return for liability) — meaning that the one who benefits from the property must bear its burdens. This is then analogized to the case of a slave whose services are bequeathed: the legatee must bear the slave's maintenance because he enjoys the benefit. The commentary then distinguishes between different types of waqf beneficiaries. If the waqf is for the poor in general (non-specific), the maintenance is obligatory from the revenue immediately because the poor are not individually liable. If the waqf is for a specific individual first and then to the poor, the maintenance falls on that individual during his lifetime, but only to the extent necessary to preserve the property in its original condition. Any improvement beyond the original state requires the consent of the beneficiaries. The passage then introduces several important issues (مسائل) regarding maintenance. The first issue: maintenance must not be delayed if needed. However, there is a nuanced ruling from al-Khaniyya: if the administrator has a charitable opportunity (like ransoming captives) and the waqf's maintenance can be safely deferred to the next year's revenue without risk of destruction, it is permissible to spend on charity now and delay maintenance. But if delay would cause obvious harm, maintenance comes first. The second issue concerns the liability of the administrator if he distributes all revenue to beneficiaries while ignoring obligatory maintenance or taxes (خراج). According to al-Dhakhira, the administrator is personally liable for the portion that should have been reserved for maintenance and taxes. A subsequent discussion, citing al-Ramli and others, debates whether the administrator can recover the money from the beneficiaries after being forced to pay from his own pocket. The preferred view is that he can recover it as long as the property remains in the beneficiaries' hands, but if consumed, there is a difference of opinion. The third issue: stipends of beneficiaries may be suspended to fund necessary maintenance. Overall, the passage demonstrates the Hanafi principle that the waqf's preservation takes precedence over current distributions, and that the administrator must balance charitable disbursement with the long-term sustainability of the waqf.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on agricultural waqf property. The mutawalli must pay this before distributing revenue.
وجه البر (wajh al-birr): A charitable cause that involves giving ownership to eligible recipients, such as ransoming captives or aiding stranded fighters.
جهات موقوف عليها (jihaat mawquf 'alayha): The beneficiaries' stipends or shares from the waqf revenue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following charitable causes is permissible to spend waqf revenue on?
A) Building a mosque.
B) Ransoming Muslim captives.
C) Constructing a public road.
D) Decorating a mosque with gold.

Key Takeaway
A mutawalli may delay maintenance for a valid charitable cause if no obvious harm, but if he distributes without reserving for maintenance, he is personally liable.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
Waqf Proceeds: Permissible Expenditure and Trustee's Liability
Explains permissible waqf spending and trustee's liability plus recourse dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of tamlik for permissible waqf expenditure and explain the trustee's liability for misallocation, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on recourse.

Core Idea
Waqf proceeds require tamlik; trustee must reserve for necessities; liability applies but recourse is disputed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies which charitable causes qualify for waqf income and what happens when a trustee distributes everything without setting aside funds for taxes or repairs. The key principle is that sadaqah requires transfer of ownership (tamlik), so non-owning entities like mosques cannot receive waqf proceeds. The passage then tackles a practical problem: if the trustee is held personally liable for misallocation, can he recover the amount from the beneficiaries? The answer involves a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute comparing the trustee to a depositary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible recipients
Analyze the text's definition of sadaqah as tamlik (transfer of ownership). Only recipients capable of owning property (e.g., human beings, not mosques or ribats) are valid. Recognize why mosques are excluded: they are not 'ahl al-tamlik'.
Sadaqah must confer ownership; building a mosque is a form of charity but not tamlik.
2
Determine the priority of waqf expenses
The text states that kharaj (land tax) and necessary repairs are 'mustathna' (excluded) from the right of beneficiaries. The trustee must reserve these before distribution. This obligation is wajib.
The rule applies even if it delays distribution.
3
Apply the liability rule
If the trustee distributes without reserving, he becomes personally liable (daman) for the shortfall. This is based on the precedent in al-Dhakhira and the principle that waqf's preservation is paramount.
Liability is independent of whether the distribution was in good faith.
4
Trace the recourse dispute
The initial analogy (qiyas) with the depositary son who spends on parents suggests no recourse. But later scholars (al-Ramli, al-Nahr) distinguish the trustee's authority, arguing for recourse if the money remains, and even if consumed.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) allows recourse as long as the funds are still with the beneficiaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف
البر. والمراد من وجه البر ههنا وجه فيه تصدق بالغلة على نوع من الفقراء نحو فك أسارى المسلمين أو إعانة الغازي المنقطع لأن هؤلاء من أهل التصدق عليهم فجاز صرف الغلة إليهم، فأما عمارة مسجد أو رباط أو نحو ذلك مما هو ليس بأهل للتمليك لا يجوز صرف لغلة إليه لأن التصدق عبارة عن التمليك فلا يصح إلا ممن هو من أهل التمليك اهـ. وظاهر أنه يجوز الصرف على المستحقين وتأخير العمارة إلى الغلة الثانية إذا لم يخف ضرر بين الثانية لو صرف المتولي على المستحقين وهناك عمارة لا يجوز تأخيرها فإنه يكون ضامناً لما في الذخيرة : إذا كانت في تلك السنة غلة ففرق القيم الغلة على المساكين ولم يمسك للخراج شيئاً فإنه يضمن حصة الخراج لأن بقدر الخراج وما يحتاج إليه الوقف من العمارة والمؤنة مستثنى عن حق الفقراء فإذا دفع إليهم ذلك ضمن اهـ. وإذا ضمن ينبغي أن لا يرجع على المستحقين بما دفعه إليهم في هذه الحالة قياساً على مودع الابن إذا أنفق على الأبوين بغير إذنه وبغير إذن القاضي فإنهم قالوا يضمن ولا رجوع له على الأبوين قالوا : لأنه ملكه بالضمان فتبين أنه دفع مال نفسه وأنه متبرع ولا رجوع فيه؛ ذكروه في آخر ماله النفقات. وعلى هذا فينبغي أنه إذا صرف على المستحقين وهناك تعمير واجب فعمر من أن لا يكون متبرعاً بالتعمير ويكون عوضاً عما لزمه بالضمان الثالثة في قطع معاليم المستحقين لأجل العمارة. قال في فتح القدير : وتقطع الجهات الموقوف عليها للعمارة إن لم فيما إذا لم يجد الآخر موضعاً يكفيه فتدبره اهـ. قوله : (وإذا ضمن ينبغي أن لا يرجع على المستحقين الخ) قال الرملي قال في النهر أقول : فيه نظر بل ما دام المدفوع قائماً في يده له الرجوع فيه لا ما إذا هلك إذ قصارى الأمر أنه هبة وفيها له الرجوع ما دامت العين قائمة بالتراضي أو بقضاء القاضي إلا لمانع فتدبره اهـ. أقول : لا وجه لجعله هبة بل هو دفع مال يستحقه غير المدفوع إليه على ظن أنه يستحقه المدفوع إليه فينبغي الرجوع قائماً أو مستهلكاً ويفرق بينه وبين نفقة مودع الابن على الأبوين بأنه مأمور بالحفظ وإنفاقه عليهما ضده إذ هو إتلاف بخلاف الدفع للمستحقين فإنه من جملة ما هو داخل تحت تصرف المتولي في الجملة والمودع لا تصرف له في الوديعة بوجه من الوجوه، فإذا ضمن ملك المدفوع منه لهما على جهة الإنفاق بخلاف المدفوع على جهة أنه حقه فإنه إذا استهلكه على هذا الوجه ولم يكن حقيقة ضمنه كالدين المظنون ملخصه أن مودع الابن دفع للإنفاق ولم يؤمر به فضمن ولا يرجع لإذنه له بها والناظر دفع على أنه استحقاقه وهو آخذه على ذلك هذا، وقد ذكر في جامع الفصولين في الثالث والثلاثين في بيان الغصب : أودعه ثياباً فجعل المودع ثوبه فيها ثم طلب الوديعة ربها فدفع الكل إليه فرب الوديعة يضمن ثوب المودع إذ من أخذ شيئاً على أنه له ولم يكن له ضمنه اهـ. ومقتضى ما ذكر أنه يضمنه المستحق هالكاً أيضاً لأنه أخذه على أنه له وليس له فيضمنه اللهم إلا أن يقال : إنه دفع الثوب ناسياً له فلم يعتبر دفعه له فكأنه أخذه بنفسه من غير دفعه له فكان متعدياً في أخذه لذلك فكانت أمانة في يده تأمل اهـ.
Book of Waqf. Righteousness: what is meant by 'aspect of righteousness' here is an aspect in which one gives charity from the produce to a type of poor people, such as ransoming Muslim captives or aiding a stranded warrior, because these are among those eligible for charity to them, so it is permissible to spend the produce on them. As for building a mosque or a ribat or the like, which are not eligible for ownership, it is not permissible to spend the produce on it because charity is a transfer of ownership, so it is only valid to someone who is eligible for ownership. And it is apparent that it is permissible to spend on the beneficiaries and to delay repairs until the second season's produce if no severe harm is feared. If the trustee spends on the beneficiaries while there is necessary repair that cannot be delayed, he becomes liable. According to al-Dhakhira: If in that year there is produce and the trustee distributes the produce to the poor and does not reserve anything for the kharaj (land tax), he guarantees the share of the kharaj because to the extent of the kharaj and what the waqf needs for repairs and maintenance is excluded from the right of the poor; so if he gives that to them, he is liable. And if he becomes liable, it is appropriate that he does not have recourse against the beneficiaries for what he paid them in this situation, by analogy to the case of a depositary son who spends on his parents without his permission and without the judge's permission: they said he is liable and has no recourse against the parents; they said: because he owns it by the guarantee, it becomes clear that he paid his own money and he is donating, and he has no recourse. They mentioned this at the end of the chapter on nafaqah. Based on this, it is appropriate that if he spends on the beneficiaries while there is obligatory repair, he should not be considered a donor regarding the repair, but rather compensation for what became binding on him by the guarantee. Third: cutting off the stipends of the beneficiaries for the sake of repairs. He said in Fath al-Qadir: The endowed shares are cut for repairs if not... when the other does not find a place sufficient for him, so reflect. His statement: (And if he is liable, it is appropriate that he does not have recourse against the beneficiaries...) al-Ramli said, [quoting] al-Nahr: I say: there is consideration; rather, as long as the paid amount remains in his hand, he has recourse to it, not if it is destroyed, because at most it is a gift, and in it he has recourse as long as the object remains, by mutual consent or by judge's ruling, except for an impediment, so reflect. I say: there is no basis to make it a gift; rather, it is payment of money that is due to someone other than the recipient, under the assumption that it is due to the recipient, so he should have recourse whether it remains or is consumed. A distinction is made between this and the case of the depositary son's spending on his parents: the depositary is ordered to preserve, and spending on them is contrary to that, as it is destruction, unlike payment to beneficiaries, which is part of what falls under the trustee's authority in general, and the depositary has no authority over the deposit in any way. So if he becomes liable, [the money] becomes owned by the one paid to as a grant, unlike payment on the basis that it is his right, because if he consumes it in that manner and it was not truly his right, he guarantees it, like a presumed debt. Summary: the depositary son paid for spending and was not ordered to do so, so he is liable and does not have recourse because he spent without permission, and the trustee paid on the basis that it was an entitlement, and the recipient took it as such. This has been mentioned in Jami' al-Fusulayn, in the thirty-third chapter on usurpation: One deposited clothes, and the depositary placed his own clothes among them, then the owner of the deposit demanded it, so he gave everything to him; the owner of the deposit guarantees the depositary's garment, because whoever takes something thinking it is his while it is not, is liable for it. The implication of what has been mentioned is that he guarantees it even if the beneficiary consumed it, because he took it thinking it was his and it was not, so he guarantees it, except if it is said: he gave the garment forgetting it, so his giving is not considered, as if he took it himself without the depositary giving, so he was transgressor in taking it, so it is a trust in his hand. Reflect.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the rules governing the expenditure of waqf proceeds and the liability of the trustee (qayyim). The author first defines the permissible 'avenues of righteousness' (wujuh al-birr) for spending waqf income: it must be given as charity (sadaqah) to those eligible to receive ownership, such as freeing captives or supporting stranded warriors. Building a mosque or ribat is not permissible because these entities cannot own property; sadaqah inherently requires transfer of ownership (tamlik). The text then addresses a common scenario: if the trustee distributes all the proceeds to the poor without setting aside funds for necessary taxes (kharaj) or repairs, he becomes personally liable for the shortfall. This is because the needs of the waqf (repairs, taxes) take precedence over distribution to beneficiaries. The ruling is based on the principle that the trustee must preserve the waqf corpus. The discussion then moves to whether the trustee, after being held liable, can recover the amount from the beneficiaries. The author presents an analogy (qiyas) to a depositary (mudi') who spends on his parents without permission: he is liable and has no recourse. However, later commentators like al-Ramli and the author of al-Nahr dispute this, arguing that the trustee should have recourse as long as the payment is still in the recipients' hands (like a gift), and even if consumed, because the trustee paid under the assumption it was due. The passage concludes with a citation from Jami' al-Fusulayn about a case of mistaken delivery in deposit, supporting the idea that the recipient is liable if he takes what is not his, analogous to the beneficiary receiving waqf proceeds that were actually needed for repairs. The overall ruling: the trustee must allocate funds for necessary expenditures before distributing to beneficiaries; if he fails and is made liable, the preferred view is that he can recover from the beneficiaries if the money is still extant, and there is disagreement if it is consumed.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghallah): The produce, revenue, or income generated from a waqf property (e.g., rent, crops).
التمليك (al-tamlik): Transfer of ownership. Charity (sadaqah) is defined as tamlik, so the recipient must be capable of owning property.
الخراج (al-kharaj): Land tax due on agricultural waqf land, which is a priority expense before distribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a valid purpose for spending waqf proceeds?
A) Building a mosque
B) Ransoming Muslim captives
C) Repairing a ribat
D) Paying salaries of imams

Key Takeaway
Waqf proceeds must be spent on recipients capable of ownership, and the trustee must reserve for necessary expenses; if he fails, he is liable but may recover from beneficiaries if the funds remain.

Cutting Beneficiaries' Stipends and the Overseer's Entitlement
Ruling on suspending stipends for repairs and on the overseer's compensation when he is a beneficiary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on cutting beneficiaries' stipends for waqf repairs (including the severe harm exception) and on the overseer's compensation based on his appointment status.

Core Idea
Stipends may be cut for repairs, but essential religious roles and the overseer's right depend on his appointment type.

Waqf administration requires balancing physical preservation and beneficiary rights. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two interconnected issues: when can stipends be suspended for repairs, and what does the overseer (nazir) deserve? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer, distinguishing between severe harm and routine cuts, and between a stipended overseer and a wage-based one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dual ruling
The passage covers two main rulings: cutting stipends for repairs and the overseer's compensation. Recognize both as separate legal questions.
2
Understand the severe harm exception
Stipends are cut unless it would cause severe harm (ḍarar bayyin), such as leaving the imam or khateeb without support. This protects the religious purpose of the waqf.
Al-Ramli explains that severe harm includes loss of imamate and khutba.
3
Analyze the overseer's status
If the waqf founder stipulated a share for the overseer, he is a beneficiary; his stipend is cut with others unless he works on repairs, then he takes a wage. If not stipulated, he only gets wage for actual work (Qadikhan's mill example).
Qadikhan's example: a trustee appointed by judge with a share gets nothing from a mill managed by someone else because no work.
4
Reconcile the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some texts (Fath al-Qadir) interpret 'unless he works' as his appointed job, others (al-Nahr) as repair work. The author (Ibn Nujaym) inclines towards repair work, so he gets wage, not his full stipend.
The author cites al-Fusulayn: if the judge orders it, the overseer can take wage for repair work.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a waqf with an imam, a khateeb, and a non-stipended overseer needing repairs, determine who gets cut and what the overseer receives. Use the severe harm exception and the overseer's wage rule.

Source Text

يخف ضرر بين، فإن خيف قدم، وأما الناظر ؛ فإن كان المشروط له من الواقف فهو كأحد المستحقين، فإذا قطعوا للعمارة قطع إلا أن يعمل فيأخذ قدر أجرته، وإن لم يعمل لا يأخذ شيئاً. قال الإمام فخر الدین قاضيخان وقف ضيعة على مواليه ومات فجعل القاضي الوقف في يد قيم وجعل له عشر الغلات مثلاً وفي الوقف طاحونة في يد رجل بالمقاطعة لا حاجة فيها إلى القيم وأصحاب هذه الطاحونة يقسمون غلتها لا يجب للقيم فيها ذلك العشر لأن القيم لا يأخذ ما يأخذه إلا بطريق الأجر فلا يستوجب الأجر بلا عمل اهـ. فهذا عندنا فيمن لم يشرط له الواقف، أما إذا شرط كان من جملة الموقوف عليهم .اهـ. فظاهره أن من عمل من المستحقين زمن العمارة فإنه يأخذ قدر أجرته لكن إذا كان مما لا يمكن ترك عمله إلا بضرر
يرجع عليهم لأخذهم ما لا يستحقونه وهو لم يدفعه متبرعاً بل ليوفيهم معلومة من غلة الوقف كما لو دفع لزوجته نفقة لا تستحقها لنشوز أو غيره له الرجوع عليها قوله : (إن لم يخف ضرر بين) قال الرملي : أي كترك الإمامة والخطبة وسيأتي بيانه قوله : (وأما الناظر فإن كان الخ) مقتضاه أن الناظر ليس ممن يخاف بقطعه ضرر ،بين والمفهوم من هذا الكلام أن من يخاف بقطعه ضرر بين كالإمام والخطيب لا يقطع معلومه، وأنه يأخذه الموظف له بتمامه وأن غيره يقطع إلا أن يعمل فيستحق أجر عمله لا المشروط له من الواقف، وهذا مستفاد من قوله تقطع الجهات الخ فمن خيف بقطعه ضرر بين لا يقطع فيبقى على حاله القديم من أخذه المشروط، ومن لا يخاف بقطعه الضرر يقطع فلا يأخذ المشروط ولو عمل بل له أجر عمله إذا عمل، وقد صرح بهذا في النهر وجعله مما أفاده المؤلف مع أن كلام المؤلف الآتي عقيب كلام الفتح يخالف هذا فتأمله قوله : (قطع إلا أن يعمل) أي يباشر العمل الذي نصب لأجله، وأما عمله في العمارة كعمل الأجير فسيأتي حكمه في المسألة التاسعة أنه لا يستحق، وسيأتي قبيل قول المتن وينزع لو خائناً بيان ما عليه من العمل وهو القيام بمصالحه من عمارة واستغلال غلات

ويؤيد ما قلنا آخراً أن قوله إلا أن يعمل إذا كان المراد به العمل الذي نصب لأجله وجعل . يستحق شيئاً بدونه وقت التعمير وبعده فلا يبقى فائدة لقوله إلا أن يعمل» تأمل . ثم رأيت في عبارة ما يعين فإنه قال : إلا أن يعمل كالفاعل والبناء ونحوهما فيأخذ قدر أجرته اهـ. قوله : (فهذا عندنا الخ الإشارة إلى ما قاله فخر الدين من مسألة الطاحون يعني أن ما ذكر من عدم وجوب العشر له إذا لم يعمل إنما هو فيمن جعل له القاضي العشر نظير عمله، أما لو جعله له الواقف فيستحق بلا عمل يعني إن لم يجعله الواقف بمقابلة عمله . قوله : (فإنه يأخذ قدر أجرته)
...severe harm is feared; if it is feared, it is given precedence. As for the overseer (nazir): if the waqf founder stipulated [a share] for him, he is like one of the beneficiaries; so if they are cut off for repairs, he is also cut off, unless he works, then he takes the amount of his wage, but if he does not work, he takes nothing. Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan said: A farm (diya') was endowed upon the freed slaves (mawali) of the founder, and he died; the judge placed the waqf in the hand of a qayyim (trustee) and gave him, for example, one-tenth of the produce. In the waqf there is a mill in the hand of a man on a contract (muqata'a) with no need for the qayyim, and the owners of this mill divide its produce; the qayyim is not entitled to that tenth for the mill, because the qayyim only takes what he takes by way of wage, so he does not deserve wage without work. This, according to us, is in the case where the waqf founder did not stipulate for him. But if he stipulated, he is among the beneficiaries. So its apparent meaning is that whoever among the beneficiaries works during the time of repairs takes the amount of his wage, but only if it is work that cannot be left without harm. He can have recourse against them for taking what they do not deserve, and he did not pay it as a donation but rather to give them their stipend from the waqf produce, just as if he paid his wife maintenance that she does not deserve due to nushuz (rebellion) or other, he has recourse against her. His statement: (If no severe harm is feared) – al-Ramli said: i.e., such as leaving the imamate and khutba, and its explanation will come. His statement: (As for the overseer, if he is...) Its implication is that the overseer is not among those whose cutting would cause severe harm. The understanding from this speech is that whoever would cause severe harm by cutting his stipend, like the imam and khateeb, his stipend is not cut, and he takes his full entitlement; but others are cut unless they work, then they deserve the wage of their work, not the stipulated amount from the waqf founder. This is derived from his statement 'the shares are cut', so whoever's cutting would endanger severe harm is not cut and remains in his previous state of taking his stipulated share; whoever's cutting would not cause harm is cut and does not take the stipulated share, even if he works, rather he has the wage of his work if he works. This has been explicitly stated in al-Nahr and made part of what the author conveyed, although the author's subsequent statement after Fath's words contradicts this, so reflect. His statement: (Unless he works) i.e., he actually performs the work for which he was appointed. As for his work in repair like an employee, its ruling will come in the ninth issue that he does not deserve it. And there will come before the author's words 'and he is removed if he is treacherous' an explanation of what work is upon him, which is looking after its interests including repair, exploitation of produce, sale, and spending what he has gathered according to the waqf founder's stipulation, and that he is not required to do the work himself except as is customary for his peers. Then it occurred to me that the apparent meaning of Fath's statement here 'unless he works' is that what is meant is his work in repair like an employee, and the meaning is that he worked by order of the judge, so he deserves the wage, so it does not contradict what will come that he does not deserve it. In al-Fusulayn: If one works in the waqf for wages, it is permissible, but fatwa is given against its permissibility because he is not suitable to be both employer and employee; but it is valid if the judge ordered him. This reinforces what we said finally: that his statement 'unless he works', if the meaning is the work for which he was appointed, then he does not deserve anything without it during and after repair, so there would be no benefit in saying 'unless he works', reflect. Then I saw in a statement that supports it: he said: 'unless he works like the doer, the builder, and the like, then he takes the amount of his wage.' His statement: (This, according to us...) refers to what Fakhr al-Din said about the mill case: i.e., what was mentioned about the non-obligation of the tenth for him if he does not work is only in the case where the judge gave him the tenth as equivalent for his work. But if the waqf founder gave it to him, he deserves without work, meaning if the waqf founder did not make it in return for his work. His statement: (He takes the amount of his wage)
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage discusses the management of waqf when necessary repairs are required. The first ruling: if the waqf needs urgent repairs and there are beneficiaries receiving stipends, their stipends may be cut to fund the repairs, unless the cutting would cause severe harm (ḍarar bayyin), such as leaving the imam or khateeb without support, which would disrupt religious services. In that case, their stipends are not cut. The second topic is the overseer (nazir): if the waqf founder stipulated a share for him in the waqf deed, he is treated as a beneficiary; his stipend is cut along with others for repairs unless he works (i.e., performs the repair work), in which case he takes the wage for his actual labor. If he does not work, he takes nothing during the repair period. The text then cites Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan's example of a waqf of a farm with a trustee (qayyim) appointed by the judge with a 10% share, but there is a mill in the waqf managed by someone else on a contract. The trustee is not entitled to any share of the mill's produce because he did no work for it; his share is only for his work as trustee. The distinction is crucial: if the waqf founder stipulated a share, it is a right of the beneficiary regardless of work; if the judge gives a share as wage, it is only due with work. The passage ends with a debate about whether the phrase 'unless he works' refers to his appointed job or repair work, and it concludes that it refers to repair work like a builder, and then he takes a fair wage. The comment from al-Fusulayn warns against the trustee being both employer and employee, but if the judge orders it, it is valid.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nazir): The overseer or supervisor of a waqf, appointed either by the waqf founder or by a judge.
المعاديل (al-ma'alim): Stipends or salaries paid to beneficiaries or employees of the waqf.
المقاطعة (al-muqata'a): A contract or lease where a person manages a waqf property (like a mill) for a fixed payment, independent of the trustee.
الضرر البين (al-ḍarar al-bayyin): Severe harm – the threshold above which cutting a stipend is prohibited. Al-Ramli gives examples: leaving the imamate or khutba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the waqf founder did not stipulate a share for the overseer (nazir), and the waqf needs repairs that require cutting stipends, what does the overseer receive?
A) He continues to receive his full stipend as usual.
B) He receives nothing unless he actually works on the repairs, in which case he takes a wage.
C) He receives his share but must return it after repairs.
D) He receives double the stipend to compensate for extra work.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances waqf preservation and beneficiary rights: stipends may be cut for repairs unless it causes severe harm, and the overseer's entitlement depends on whether he was made a beneficiary by the waqf founder.

Cutting Salaries of Waqf Personnel During Construction
Ruling on cutting salaries during waqf construction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on cutting salaries of waqf personnel during construction and apply the distinction between those whose removal causes severe harm and those who do not.

Core Idea
Salary continues only if removal causes severe harm; others must work to earn during construction.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies when salaries of waqf functionaries may be suspended during construction or repair. The key principle is whether the removal of a person from his post would cause severe harm (darar bayyin) to the waqf's functioning. The passage distinguishes between essential personnel like the imam and khatib, whose salaries continue, and others like the nazir, who forfeit the conditional stipend unless they actually work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Salaries of waqf personnel are cut during construction unless the removal would cause severe harm (darar bayyin) to the waqf's functions.
2
Define 'severe harm' (darar bayyin)
This is harm such as leaving the imamate or sermon unattended, where no one else can fill the role without damage.
Al-Ramli explains it as leaving the imamate and khutba.
3
Contrast the nazir's case
The nazir (supervisor) is not considered essential; his salary is cut. However, if he works in construction, he receives wages for that work, not the conditional stipend.
The passage quotes Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan on a mill example.
4
Distinguish between types of nazir
If the waqf founder stipulated the nazir as a beneficiary, he is treated like other beneficiaries and his salary is cut unless he works. If not stipulated, he is like a hired agent and only gets wages for work done.
5
Consider the effect of a judge's order
If the nazir works in construction by the judge's order, he deserves wages; otherwise, he may not be entitled even to wages if the judge did not authorize it.
The author mentions a fatwa against permissibility of being both employer and employee without judge's order.

There is a fear of severe harm. If there is fear, it is given precedence. As for the supervisor: if the condition is from the waqf founder, he is like one of the beneficiaries. So if they are cut off for construction, he is cut off unless he works, then he takes the amount of his wage. And if he does not work, he takes nothing. Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan said: He made a waqf of a farm for his clients, and he died. So the judge placed the waqf in the hand of a steward and assigned him for example one-tenth of the yields. In the waqf there is a mill in the hand of a man by contract, no need for the steward. The owners of this mill divide its yield. The one-tenth is not obligatory for the steward in it because the steward only takes what he takes by way of wage, so he does not deserve the wage without work. End quote. So this is with us when the waqf founder did not stipulate for him. But if he stipulated, then he is among the beneficiaries. End quote. So its apparent meaning is that whoever among the beneficiaries works during the time of construction takes the amount of his wage, but only if his work cannot be left except with harm. They are returned upon them because they took what they do not deserve, and he did not pay it as a gift, but rather to pay them their stipend from the produce of the waqf, just as if he paid his wife maintenance she does not deserve due to nushuz or other, he has recourse to take it back. His saying: (If there is no fear of severe harm). Al-Ramli said: i.e. like leaving the imamate and sermon, and its explanation will come. His saying: (As for the supervisor, if he is...) its implication is that the supervisor is not among those whose removal is feared of severe harm. The understood meaning from this speech is that whoever among those whose removal is feared of severe harm, like the imam and khatib, his stipend is not cut off, and he takes it in full. Others are cut off, unless they work, then they deserve the wage of their work, not the stipend from the waqf. This is derived from his saying: The positions are cut off, etc. So whoever is feared of severe harm from his removal is not cut off, so he remains on his former state of taking the stipend. Whoever is not feared of harm from his removal is cut off, so he does not take the stipend, even if he works; rather he has the wage of his work if he works. This is explicitly stated in al-Nahr and he made it among the benefits of the author, although the author's statement following the statement of al-Fath contradicts this, so contemplate. His saying: (Cut off unless he works) i.e. he personally performs the work for which he was appointed. As for his work in the construction like the work of a hired laborer, its ruling will come in issue nine that he does not deserve it. And before the text's saying 'and he is removed if he is treacherous,' there will be an explanation of what work he is required to do: managing the interests including construction, exploiting the produce, selling and disbursing what has been collected according to the waqf founder's conditions, and that he is not required to do the work himself except as is customary for his peers. Then it occurred to me that apparently the meaning of al-Fath's statement here 'unless he works' is his work in construction like the work of a hired laborer, and it means that he worked by order of the judge, so he deserves the wage, so it does not contradict what will come that he does not deserve it. In al-Fusulayn: If one works in the waqf for wages, it is permissible, and the fatwa is against its permissibility because he cannot be both employer and employee, but it is valid if the judge ordered it. End quote. This supports our last statement: if 'unless he works' refers to the work for which he was appointed, he would deserve something without it during construction and after, so there would be no benefit in 'unless he works'; contemplate. Then I saw in an expression what confirms: he said unless he works like the doer, builder, etc., taking the amount of his wage. End quote. His saying: (So this is with us etc.) refers to what Fakhr al-Din said about the mill issue, meaning that what was mentioned of the one-tenth not being obligatory for him if he does not work is only when the judge assigned the one-tenth as a wage for his work. But if the waqf founder assigned it to him, he deserves it without work, meaning if the waqf founder did not make it in exchange for his work. His saying: (He takes the amount of his wage) in the case of the imam and khatib, the stipulated stipend is not considered during construction. So according to this, if the direct worker and the overseer work in construction, they are given only the amount of their work's wage. As for those whose removal does not cause severe harm, they are given nothing at all during construction.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses the ruling on cutting off salaries of waqf personnel during the period of construction and repair. The key distinction is whether the removal of a person from his position would cause severe harm (ضرر بین). Those whose removal causes such harm, like the imam of a mosque or the khatib, are not cut off and continue to receive their full stipend. Others, especially the nazir (supervisor) who is not essential, are cut off from the stipend during construction; they only receive wages if they actually perform work, but not the conditional stipend. The passage clarifies that the nazir, if appointed by the waqf founder as a beneficiary, is like other beneficiaries. However, if the nazir works in the construction (like a hired laborer), he deserves the wage for that work. The author cites opinions from Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan and al-Ramli to support these distinctions. The central principle is that payment from waqf revenue is for actual service; during construction, the regular service is suspended, so only essential personnel continue to receive their stipend, while others must work to earn anything.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nazir): The supervisor of a waqf, appointed by the founder or judge.
ضرر بين (darar bayyin): Severe harm that would result from removing a functionary, such as leaving the imamate or sermon.
المعلوم (al-ma'lum): The stipend or salary assigned to a waqf functionary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is cut off entirely.
B) He receives half of his salary.
C) He continues to receive his full salary.
D) He only gets a wage if he works.

Key Takeaway
During waqf construction, essential personnel whose removal causes severe harm retain their salary; others are cut off but may earn wages for actual work.

Borrowing for Waqf Repairs: General Rule and Necessity Exception
This passage explores the permissibility of borrowing for waqf repairs when no income is available.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on borrowing for waqf repairs and apply the conditions under which borrowing becomes permissible due to necessity.

Core Idea
Borrowing for waqf repairs is generally prohibited; only necessity and judicial authorization allow it.

Imagine a waqf mosque with a leaking roof but no income to fix it. Can the steward borrow money? The general rule says no, because the waqf has no liability and the beneficiaries are numerous. But necessity may change that. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the exceptional cases where borrowing is permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State the baseline: borrowing for waqf repairs is not permissible. Understand the reasoning: waqf has no liability and beneficiaries are too many to sue.
This is the qiyas argument.
2
Recognize the necessity exception
Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far reports that qiyas is abandoned when there is real need. The passage gives two examples: crop eaten by locusts needing harvest funds, and sultan demanding kharaj tax.
The first example is straightforward; the second causes dispute.
3
Analyze the kharaj problem
Understand why borrowing for kharaj is conceptually problematic: if the land has income, sell it; if not, only the corpus exists, which is not owned by the poor. The debt cannot be on non-beneficiary property.
A resolution is possible only if income exists but cannot be liquidated immediately.
4
Apply the procedural safeguard
The preferred opinion: the steward should seek the judge's order before borrowing. Only if the judge is far away may he borrow independently.
This ensures accountability and broad authority.
5
Compare to the guardian-orphan analogy
Note that the steward is not like a guardian for an orphan; the orphan has a clear liability, so the guardian can even buy on credit without necessity.
This highlights the unique nature of waqf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة في الاستدانة لأجل العمارة حيث لم يكن غلة. قال في الذخيرة قال هلال : إذا احتاجت الصدقة إلى العمارة وليس في يد القيم ما يعمرها فليس له أن يستدين عليها لأن الدين لا يجب ابتداء إلا في الذمة وليس للوقف ذمة، والفقراء وإن كانت لهم ذمة إلا أنهم لكثرتهم لا تتصور مطالبتهم فلا يثبت الدين باستدانة القيم إلا عليه ودين يجب عليه لا يملك قضاءه غلة على الفقراء. وعن الفقيه أبي جعفر أن القياس من هذا لكن يترك القياس فيما فيه ضرورة نحو أن يكون في أرض الوقف زرع يأكله الجراد ويحتاج إلى النفقة لجمع الزرع أو طالبه السلطان بالخراج جاز له الاستدانة لأن القياس يترك للضرورة. قال: والأحوط في هذه الصورة كونها بأمر الحاكم لأن ولاية الحاكم أعم في مصالح المسلمين من ولايته إلا أن يكون بعيداً عن الحاكم ولا يمكنه الحضور فلا بأس بأن يستدين بنفسه، وهذا الذي روي عن الفقيه أبي جعفر مشكل لأنه جمع بين أكل الجراد والزرع وبين الخراج. وتتصور الاستدانة في أكل الجراد الزرع لأن الزرع مال للفقراء وهذا الدين إنما يستدان لحاجتهم فأمكن إيجاب الدين في مالهم، فأما باب الخراج فلا يتصور لأنه إن كان في الأرض غلة فلا ضرورة إلى الاستدانة لأن الغلة تباع ويؤدى منها الخراج، وإن لم يكن في الأض غلة فليس هنا إلا رقبة الوقف ورقبة الوقف ليست للفقراء، ولا يستقيم إيجاب دين يحتاج إليه الفقراء في مال ليس لهم فهذا الفصل مشكل من هذا الوجه إلا أن يكون تصوير المسألة فيما إذا كان في الأرض غلة وكان بيعها متعذراً في الحال وقد طولب بالخراج قالوا: ليس قيم الوقف في الاستدانة على الوقف كالوصي في الاستدانة على اليتيم له ذمة صحيحة وهو معلوم فتتصور ،مطالبته، ألا ترى أن للوصي أن يشتري لليتيم شيئاً بنسيئة من غير ضرورة. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث قيم وقف طلب منه الجبايات والخراج وليس في يده من مال الوقف شيء وأراد أن يستدين فهذا على وجهين : إن أمر الواقف بالاستدانة فله ذلك، وإن لم يأمره بالاستدانة فقد اختلف المشايخ فيه قال الصدر الشهيد : والمختار ما قاله الفقيه أبو الليث إذا لم يكن للاستدانة بد يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي حتى يأمره بالاستدانة ثم يرجع في غلة الوقف
The fourth: On borrowing for the sake of construction when there is no income. It is said in al-Dhakhira, Hilaal said: If the charity needs construction and the steward has nothing to build with, it is not permissible for him to borrow because debt is not initially obligated except on a person's liability, and a waqf has no liability. The poor, even if they have liability, are so many that suing them is inconceivable, so debt is not established by the steward's borrowing except against him, and a debt that is obligatory on him he cannot discharge from the produce of the poor. From al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: the qiyas is this, but qiyas is abandoned when there is necessity, such as if in the waqf land there is a crop that locusts eat, and there is need for spending to gather the crop, or if the sultan demands the kharaj tax; then it is permissible for him to borrow because qiyas is abandoned for necessity. He said: The most precautionary in this case is that it be by order of the judge, because the judge's authority over the Muslims' interests is more general than his authority, unless he is far from the judge and cannot attend, then it is permissible for him to borrow himself. This narrated from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far is problematic because he combined locust eating of the crop with kharaj. Borrowing is conceivable for locust eating the crop because the crop is property of the poor, and this debt is borrowed for their need, so it is possible to impose the debt on their property. As for the issue of kharaj, it is not conceivable because if there is income from the land, there is no need to borrow, since the income is sold and kharaj paid from it. If there is no income from the land, then there is only the corpus of the waqf, and the corpus is not for the poor. It is not correct to impose a debt needed by the poor on property that is not theirs. So this section is problematic from this angle, unless the issue is depicted when there is income from the land but its sale is difficult at the time and the kharaj is demanded. They said: The waqf steward is not like a guardian borrowing for an orphan; the orphan has a valid liability that is known, so suing him is conceivable. Do you not see that the guardian may buy for the orphan on credit without necessity? In the Fatawa of Abu al-Layth: A waqf steward was demanded the taxes and kharaj and had no waqf money in hand and wanted to borrow. This is two-sided: if the waqf founder ordered borrowing, it is allowed; if not, the scholars differed. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: The chosen is what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: if there is no alternative to borrowing, he should raise the matter to the judge until he orders him to borrow, then he recovers from the waqf income.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the fourth issue concerning waqf: borrowing for repairs when there is no income. The general rule is that borrowing is not allowed because the waqf has no liability and the beneficiaries are not collectively liable. However, al-Faqih Abu Ja'far reports that qiyas is set aside in cases of necessity. Two examples: (1) a crop on waqf land is being eaten by locusts and money is needed to harvest it; (2) the sultan demands kharaj (land tax). In these cases, borrowing is allowed. The author notes that the case of locusts is straightforward because the crop belongs to the poor, so debt can be imposed on their property. The case of kharaj is problematic because if the land has income, no borrowing is needed; if no income, only the corpus exists, which is not owned by the poor, so debt cannot be imposed on it. A possible solution is when there is income but it is not immediately liquid. The passage also compares the steward to a guardian: the guardian can buy for an orphan on credit without necessity, but this is not analogous. The preferred opinion (from Abu al-Layth and al-Sadr al-Shahid) is that if borrowing is unavoidable, the steward should seek the judge's order first; if the judge is far away, he may borrow himself. If the waqf founder permitted borrowing in the deed, it is allowed.

Key Terms
الاستدانة (al-istidana): Borrowing money for the purpose of repairing or maintaining waqf property.
القيم (al-qayyim): The steward or caretaker of the waqf, responsible for its upkeep and collection of income.
الضرورة (al-darura): Necessity that overrides the general prohibition of borrowing, such as preventing loss of waqf assets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the general ruling on a steward borrowing for waqf repairs?
A) It is always permissible.
B) It is not permissible because the waqf has no liability.
C) It is permissible only for personal use.
D) It is permissible if approved by the beneficiaries.

Key Takeaway
Borrowing for waqf repairs is generally prohibited; it becomes permissible only under necessity and preferably with a judge's order to protect all parties.

Borrowing for Waqf Maintenance: General Rule and Necessity Exception
Explaining the ruling on borrowing for waqf maintenance and the necessity exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on borrowing for waqf maintenance and identify the two recognized exceptions (founder's permission and qadi's order in necessity).

Core Idea
A waqf has no legal personality (dhimmah), so its custodian cannot borrow against it; necessity may permit borrowing but only with proper authorization.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical question in waqf management: can the custodian (qayyim) borrow money to maintain the waqf property when funds are lacking? The Hanafi school's rule is strict: borrowing is generally prohibited because debt requires a legal personality (dhimmah), which the waqf lacks. However, necessity (darura) creates an exception, but subject to important procedural safeguards. The discussion includes intra-Hanafi differences and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is borrowing (istidana) by the waqf custodian for maintenance expenses. The general ruling is that it is prohibited (makruh tahriman) because waqf has no dhimmah and the debt would fall on the custodian personally.
The prohibition is based on qiyas: debt requires a legal personality.
2
Understand the qiyas underlying the prohibition
The qiyas: asl is a person borrowing for himself (debt on his dhimmah), far' is the custodian borrowing for waqf. The illa is that dhimmah is necessary for debt, which waqf lacks. Therefore, the custodian cannot impose debt on the waqf.
Qiyas is clear but exceptions due to necessity are considered.
3
Analyze the necessity exception proposed by Abu Ja'far
Abu Ja'far argues that qiyas is abandoned in cases of necessity, such as locusts eating the crop or urgent kharaj demand. However, the author finds the kharaj example problematic because the waqf's land income (if any) should be used first; if no income, the corpus is not the poor's property.
The locust example is more straightforward: the crop belongs to the poor, so borrowing for their need is logical.
4
Explore the requirement for qadi's permission (Abu al-Layth's view)
The preferred view as per Abu al-Layth, al-Sadr al-Shahid, and al-Khulasah is that the custodian must seek the qadi's permission before borrowing in necessity, unless the founder has already authorized it. The qadi has broader authority over Muslim interests.
This is the mufta bihi position: procedural safeguard to prevent misuse.
5
Distinguish the custodian from an orphan's guardian
The text notes that an orphan's guardian can borrow for the orphan because the orphan has a clear dhimmah. The waqf custodian does not have the same authority because waqf lacks legal personality.
This emphasizes the unique nature of waqf as an inalienable charitable trust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في الذخيرة قال هلال : إذا احتاجت الصدقة إلى العمارة وليس في يد القيم ما يعمرها فليس له أن يستدين عليها لأن الدين لا يجب ابتداء إلا في الذمة وليس للوقف ذمة، والفقراء وإن كانت لهم ذمة إلا أنهم لكثرتهم لا تتصور مطالبتهم فلا يثبت الدين باستدانة القيم إلا عليه ودين يجب عليه لا يملك قضاءه غلة على الفقراء. وعن الفقيه أبي جعفر أن القياس من هذا لكن يترك القياس فيما فيه ضرورة نحو أن يكون في أرض الوقف زرع يأكله الجراد ويحتاج إلى النفقة لجمع الزرع أو طالبه السلطان بالخراج جاز له الاستدانة لأن القياس يترك للضرورة. قال: والأحوط في هذه الصورة كونها بأمر الحاكم لأن ولاية الحاكم أعم في مصالح المسلمين من ولايته إلا أن يكون بعيداً عن الحاكم ولا يمكنه الحضور فلا بأس بأن يستدين بنفسه، وهذا الذي روي عن الفقيه أبي جعفر مشكل لأنه جمع بين أكل الجراد والزرع وبين الخراج. وتتصور الاستدانة في أكل الجراد الزرع لأن الزرع مال للفقراء وهذا الدين إنما يستدان لحاجتهم فأمكن إيجاب الدين في مالهم، فأما باب الخراج فلا يتصور لأنه إن كان في الأرض غلة فلا ضرورة إلى الاستدانة لأن الغلة تباع ويؤدى منها الخراج، وإن لم يكن في الأض غلة فليس هنا إلا رقبة الوقف ورقبة الوقف ليست للفقراء، ولا يستقيم إيجاب دين يحتاج إليه الفقراء في مال ليس لهم فهذا الفصل مشكل من هذا الوجه إلا أن يكون تصوير المسألة فيما إذا كان في الأرض غلة وكان بيعها متعذراً في الحال وقد طولب بالخراج قالوا: ليس قيم الوقف في الاستدانة على الوقف كالوصي في الاستدانة على اليتيم له ذمة صحيحة وهو معلوم فتتصور مطالبته، ألا ترى أن للوصي أن يشتري لليتيم شيئاً بنسيئة من غير ضرورة. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث قيم وقف طلب منه الجبايات والخراج وليس في يده من مال الوقف شيء وأراد أن يستدين فهذا على وجهين : إن أمر الواقف بالاستدانة فله ذلك، وإن لم يأمره بالاستدانة فقد اختلف المشايخ فيه قال الصدر الشهيد : والمختار ما قاله الفقيه أبو الليث إذا لم يكن للاستدانة بد يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي حتى يأمره بالاستدانة ثم يرجع في غلة الوقف لأن للقاضي هذه الولاية وإن كان لها بد ليس للقاضي هذه الولاية. وفي واقعات الناطفي : المتولي إذا أراد أن يستدين على الوقف ليجعل ذلك في ثمن البذر؛ إن أراد ذلك بأمر القاضي فله ذلك بلا خلاف لأن القاضي يملك الاستدانة على الوقف فيملك المتولي ذلك بإذن القاضي، وإن أراد ذلك بغير أمر القاضي ففيه روايتان. وصرح في الخلاصة بأن الأصح ما قاله الفقيه أبو الليث
He said in al-Dhakhirah: Hilal said: If the charity (waqf) needs maintenance and the custodian has no waqf funds to maintain it, he may not borrow against it because debt is not initially obligatory except upon a dhimmah (legal capacity) and the waqf has no dhimmah. The poor (beneficiaries) have dhimmah, but due to their large number, suing them is not conceivable, so debt is not established by the custodian's borrowing except against him, and a debt owed by him cannot be paid from the waqf's produce for the poor. From al-Faqih Abu Ja‘far: analogy (qiyas) is like this, but qiyas is abandoned in cases of necessity, such as if there is a crop in the waqf land that locusts are eating and it needs expenditure to harvest the crop, or if the Sultan demands kharaj (land tax), then borrowing is permitted because qiyas is abandoned for necessity. He said: The most precautionary in this scenario is that it be by the order of the judge, because the judge's authority is more general in the interests of Muslims than his authority, unless he is far from the judge and cannot attend, then there is no harm in his borrowing himself. This reported from al-Faqih Abu Ja‘far is problematic because it combined eating of locusts with the crop and with kharaj. Borrowing for locusts eating the crop is conceivable because the crop is the property of the poor, and this debt is borrowed for their need, so it is possible to impose debt on their property. As for the matter of kharaj, it is not conceivable because if there is produce in the land, there is no need for borrowing since the produce can be sold and the kharaj paid from it; if there is no produce in the land, there is only the corpus of the waqf, and the corpus is not for the poor, so it is not correct to impose a debt needed by the poor on property that is not theirs. This section is problematic from this aspect, unless the scenario is depicted as when there is produce in the land but its sale is temporarily difficult and he has been demanded for kharaj. They said: The custodian of waqf is not like the guardian of an orphan in borrowing against the waqf; the orphan has a valid dhimmah and is known, so suing him is conceivable. Do you not see that the guardian may buy something on credit for the orphan without necessity? And in the Fatawa of Abu al-Layth: The custodian of a waqf who is demanded taxes and kharaj and has no waqf funds in hand and wants to borrow: this is of two types: if the waqf founder ordered borrowing, he may do so; if he did not order it, the scholars differed. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: The chosen is what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: if there is no alternative to borrowing, he should refer the matter to the judge so that he orders him to borrow, then he recovers from the waqf's produce because the judge has this authority; if there is an alternative, the judge does not have this authority. And in Waqi‘at al-Natif: The mutawalli (custodian) who wants to borrow against the waqf to use it for the price of seeds: if he wants that by the judge's order, he may do so without dispute, because the judge has the authority to borrow against the waqf, so the mutawalli may do so with the judge's permission; if he wants to do so without the judge's order, there are two narrations. And in al-Khulasah it is stated that the correct is what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on borrowing (istidana) for waqf maintenance. The text presents the general rule: a waqf custodian (qayyim) cannot borrow against the waqf because debt requires a legal personality (dhimmah), which the waqf lacks. The beneficiaries (fuqara') have dhimmah but are too numerous to be sued, so the debt would only be on the custodian personally. However, necessity (darura) allows an exception to qiyas. Al-Faqih Abu Ja‘far permits borrowing in cases like locusts eating the crop or kharaj demand, but the author finds his combination problematic. For locusts, the crop is the poor's property, so borrowing for their need is logical; for kharaj, if there is produce, no need to borrow; if no produce, the corpus is not the poor's property, so debt cannot be imposed. A resolution is when produce exists but sale is temporarily difficult. The preferable view of Abu al-Layth is that without a founder's order, the custodian must seek the judge's permission, as the judge has broader authority. This is supported by al-Khulasah and Waqi‘at al-Natif. The passage emphasizes that the custodian's position is weaker than a guardian of an orphan because the orphan has a clear legal personality.

Key Terms
قيم الوقف (qayyim al-waqf): The custodian or manager of a waqf property.
استدانة (istidana): Borrowing money or taking a loan.
ضرورة (darura): Necessity that permits deviation from the general prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, when may a waqf custodian borrow without the qadi's permission?
A) In any case of necessity
B) Only if the waqf founder explicitly ordered borrowing
C) Never, even with necessity
D) Only if the beneficiaries agree

Key Takeaway
The general rule is that a waqf custodian cannot borrow against the waqf; necessity justifies borrowing only with founder's permission or qadi's order.

The Beam Precaution: Avoiding Conflict of Interest in Waqf Purchases
Explaining the precautionary method for a waqf custodian to use his own property for the waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi precautionary method for a waqf custodian to contribute his own property to the waqf and explain why this method avoids conflict of interest.

Core Idea
A custodian must sell his beam to a third party before buying it for the waqf to avoid self-dealing.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a delicate situation: a waqf custodian who wants to use his own property for the waqf. Direct purchase from oneself would be problematic. The Hanafi solution is a three-step precaution that preserves transparency and avoids any suspicion of self-benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Why can't the custodian directly insert his own beam into the waqf building? Because it would be a self-dealing transaction, creating a conflict of interest.
2
State the precautionary method
The method: sell the beam to a third party, then buy it from that third party for the waqf, then insert it.
The third party must be a genuine outsider.
3
Analyse the legal effect
This converts the beam from personal property into waqf property via a valid sale, avoiding any direct self-benefit.
It is a valid transaction (sale) between two consenting parties.
4
Note the terminology
The text uses 'ihtiyat' (precaution), indicating this is a recommended practice to avoid doubt, not an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة في مسألة الجذع والاحتياط أن يبيع الجذع من آخر ثم يشتريه لأجل الوقف ثم يدخله في دار الوقف .اهـ. و فسر قاضيخان الاستدانة على الوقف بتفسيرين فقال في الثاني وتفسير الاستدانة بما ذكر إنما هو فيما إذا لم يكن في يده شيء من الغلة، وأما إذا كان في يده شيء منها واشترى شيئاً للوقف ونقد الثمن من ماله جاز له أن يرجع بذلك من غلته، وإن لم يكن بأمر القاضي كالوكيل بالشراء إذا نقد الثمن من ماله فإنه يجوز له الرجوع به على موكله. وقال في الأول أن لا يكون للوقف غلة فيحتاج إلى القرض والاستدانة، أما إذا كان للوقف غلة فأنفق من مال نفسه لإصلاح الوقف فإن له أن يرجع في غلة الوقف اهـ . وفي القنية برقم (يو)، قيم أنفق في عمارة المسجد من مال نفسه ثم رجع بمثله اهـ.
And in al-Khulasah regarding the beam case: The precaution is that he sell the beam to another, then buy it for the sake of the waqf, then insert it into the waqf building. He said: Qadikhan interpreted borrowing (istidana) against the waqf in two ways. In the second interpretation: The interpretation of borrowing as mentioned is only when he has no produce (ghalla) in hand. But if he has some produce in hand and he bought something for the waqf and paid the price from his own money, he may recover that from the produce, even if it was not by the judge's order, like an agent for purchase who pays the price from his money may recover it from his principal. In the first interpretation: That the waqf has no produce, so he needs a loan and borrowing. As for if the waqf has produce and he spent from his own money to repair the waqf, he may recover it from the waqf's produce. And in al-Qunyah, with number 10: A custodian who spent on the mosque's repair from his own money then recovered the equivalent.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage provides two additional rulings within the same discussion on waqf maintenance. First, the precautionary method for a custodian who wants to insert his own beam into a waqf building: he should sell the beam to a third party, then buy it back for the waqf, avoiding direct conflict of interest. Second, Qadikhan clarifies that 'istidana' (borrowing) has two meanings. In one sense, it refers to when the waqf has no produce, so the custodian needs to borrow externally. In another sense, it applies when the waqf has produce but the custodian uses his own money for expenses; in that case, he can recover from the produce even without a judge's order, similar to an agent recovering from his principal. This distinction is important because it determines whether the custodian needs prior permission. The text from al-Qunyah supports that a custodian who spends his own money on mosque repairs can recover the equivalent from waqf revenue.

Key Terms
الجذع (al-jadh'): A wooden beam or pole used in construction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the beam case, what is the first step of the Hanafi precaution?
A) Buy the beam from a third party.
B) Sell the beam to a third party.
C) Get the judge's permission.
D) Insert the beam directly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ihtiyat for a waqf custodian contributing personal property is to sell it to a third party and then buy it for the waqf, avoiding conflict of interest.

Qadikhan's Two Interpretations of Istidana: When Can a Custodian Recover Personal Expenses from Waqf Revenue?
Clarifying Qadikhan's two interpretations of istidana regarding waqf expenses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Qadikhan's two interpretations of istidana and determine when a waqf custodian may recover his personal expenses from waqf produce without a judge's order.

Core Idea
Istidana can mean either borrowing when the waqf has no income, or spending personal money when the waqf has income and then recovering it.

This passage delves into Qadikhan's clarification of the term 'istidana' (borrowing) against waqf. He identifies two distinct scenarios: one where the waqf has no produce, requiring external borrowing; and another where the waqf has produce but the custodian uses his own money and recovers it. This distinction has important consequences for whether the custodian needs prior permission.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ambiguity
The term 'istidana' can be interpreted differently; Qadikhan provides two meanings.
2
Identify the first interpretation
The waqf has no ghalla (produce), so the custodian needs to borrow externally (likely with qadi permission).
This is the literal meaning of borrowing.
3
Identify the second interpretation
The waqf has ghalla, and the custodian spends his own money, then recovers from the ghalla without a judge's order – analogous to an agent.
This is a figurative use of 'istidana' meaning spending with intention of reimbursement.
4
Note the consequence
In the second interpretation, no prior permission is needed; the custodian can recover expenses directly from waqf revenue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة في مسألة الجذع والاحتياط أن يبيع الجذع من آخر ثم يشتريه لأجل الوقف ثم يدخله في دار الوقف .اهـ. و فسر قاضيخان الاستدانة على الوقف بتفسيرين فقال في الثاني وتفسير الاستدانة بما ذكر إنما هو فيما إذا لم يكن في يده شيء من الغلة، وأما إذا كان في يده شيء منها واشترى شيئاً للوقف ونقد الثمن من ماله جاز له أن يرجع بذلك من غلته، وإن لم يكن بأمر القاضي كالوكيل بالشراء إذا نقد الثمن من ماله فإنه يجوز له الرجوع به على موكله. وقال في الأول أن لا يكون للوقف غلة فيحتاج إلى القرض والاستدانة، أما إذا كان للوقف غلة فأنفق من مال نفسه لإصلاح الوقف فإن له أن يرجع في غلة الوقف اهـ . وفي القنية برقم (يو)، قيم أنفق في عمارة المسجد من مال نفسه ثم رجع بمثله اهـ.
And in al-Khulasah regarding the beam case: The precaution is that he sell the beam to another, then buy it for the sake of the waqf, then insert it into the waqf building. He said: Qadikhan interpreted borrowing (istidana) against the waqf in two ways. In the second interpretation: The interpretation of borrowing as mentioned is only when he has no produce (ghalla) in hand. But if he has some produce in hand and he bought something for the waqf and paid the price from his own money, he may recover that from the produce, even if it was not by the judge's order, like an agent for purchase who pays the price from his money may recover it from his principal. In the first interpretation: That the waqf has no produce, so he needs a loan and borrowing. As for if the waqf has produce and he spent from his own money to repair the waqf, he may recover it from the waqf's produce. And in al-Qunyah, with number 10: A custodian who spent on the mosque's repair from his own money then recovered the equivalent.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage provides two additional rulings within the same discussion on waqf maintenance. First, the precautionary method for a custodian who wants to insert his own beam into a waqf building: he should sell the beam to a third party, then buy it back for the waqf, avoiding direct conflict of interest. Second, Qadikhan clarifies that 'istidana' (borrowing) has two meanings. In one sense, it refers to when the waqf has no produce, so the custodian needs to borrow externally. In another sense, it applies when the waqf has produce but the custodian uses his own money for expenses; in that case, he can recover from the produce even without a judge's order, similar to an agent recovering from his principal. This distinction is important because it determines whether the custodian needs prior permission. The text from al-Qunyah supports that a custodian who spends his own money on mosque repairs can recover the equivalent from waqf revenue.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghalla): The produce or revenue generated by the waqf property.
الاستدانة (al-istidana): Borrowing or the act of spending personal money with intention of reimbursement, as interpreted by Qadikhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Qadikhan's interpretation, when does a waqf custodian need to obtain a judge's order before spending personal money for waqf expenses?
A) When the waqf has produce.
B) When the waqf has no produce.
C) Never.
D) Always.

Key Takeaway
Qadikhan's distinction: 'istidana' can mean borrowing when waqf has no income, or personal spending with later reimbursement when it does; only the former requires prior permission.
