Priority of Ritual Functionaries in Waqf Distribution
Intra-Hanafi dispute over prioritization of ritual functionaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on prioritizing arbab al-sha'a'ir over other beneficiaries in waqf distribution when income is limited, and evaluate the counter-argument based on qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Core Idea
Essential waqf functionaries are prioritized like maintenance, overriding the founder's stipulation of equality when funds are tight.

When a waqf's income is insufficient to cover all its beneficiaries, a conflict arises between the founder's stipulation of equality and the need to sustain the waqf's core functions. This lesson unpacks a Hanafi dispute: should the imam, teacher, and similar ritual functionaries be paid first, even if the founder ordered equal shares? The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the arguments for and against, and settles on the priority of those who perform the waqf's essential rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source texts
First, locate the primary quotation from al-Hawi al-Qudsi and the commentary from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. Note the key phrase: 'that which is started with is maintenance, then what is closer to maintenance and more general for benefit, like the imam...'
al-Hawi lists a hierarchy: maintenance first, then functionaries (imam, mudarris), then minor items.
2
Understand the claimed analogy
The commentator of al-Ashbah argues that just as maintenance is prioritized regardless of the founder's stipulation, so too are the 'people of rituals' (arbab al-sha'a'ir), because they provide general benefit similar to maintenance.
This is a qiyas (analogy) between maintenance and rituals.
3
Analyze the objector's critique
The objector raises two points: (1) The analogy is flawed because maintenance preserves the physical asset, while rituals do not; (2) The continuation of al-Hawi's text restricts priority to cases where the founder did not specify fixed amounts.
The objector calls this 'qiyas ma'a al-fariq' (analogy with a difference).
4
Evaluate the response to the objection
The defender responds: the shared element is 'general benefit' (al-naf' al-'amm), not physical preservation. Both maintenance and rituals benefit the waqf's purpose. The restriction in al-Hawi refers to the trustee's discretion, not to the principle of priority.
Support is drawn from Quniyat al-Fatawa and the fatwa of Hamid Efendi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sides with al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. The operative ruling: arbab al-sha'a'ir are given priority over other beneficiaries even if the founder stipulated equality, and the trustee may exercise discretion when amounts are not fixed.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف قال في الحاوي القدسي من كتاب الوقف بما لفظه : الذي يبدأ به من ارتفاع الوقف عمارته شرط أو لا، ثم ما هو أقرب للعمارة وأعم للمصلحة كالإمام للمسجد والمدرس للمدرسة يصرف إليهم قدر كفايتهم، ثم السراج والبساط كذلك اهـ. قال شيخنا رحمه الله تعالى في كتابه المسمى بالأشباه والنظائر من كتاب الوقف : ظاهر هذه العبارة أن المقدم في الصرف الإمام والمدرس والوقاد والفراش ومن كان بمعناهم لتعبيره بالكاف، وظاهرها يفيد أيضاً تقديم من ذكرناه ولو شرط الواقف الاستواء عند الضيق لا جعلهم كالعمارة، ولو شرط الواقف استواء العمارة بالمستحقين لم يعتبر شرطه وإنما تقدم عليهم فكذا هم .اهـ. ما ذكره الشيخ رحمه الله تعالى . فعلى مقتضى ما أفاده من أن عبارة الحاوي تفيد أن أرباب الشعائر يقدمون على غيرهم من المستحقين وأن شرط الواقف الاستواء عند الضيق يجب أن يقال تقدم أرباب الشعائر في هذا الوقف المسؤول ، بالأولى لأن في حالة شرط استواء أرباب الشعائر بغيرهم لا تحرم أرباب الشعائر بالكلية ومع ذلك ألغى شرط الاستواء، فإلغاؤه في حالة قد يحرمون فيها بالكلية وهي حالة شرط تقديم أهل الحرمين عليهم بتقدير أن لا يفضل شيء لأرباب الشعائر عليهم بالأولى، ثم توقف فيما أفاده شيخنا رحمه الله تعالى بعض مشايخنا أطال الله بقاءه، وحاصل توقفه أنه قال : لا نسلم أولاً أن يقاس حكم أرباب الشعائر على حكم العمارة لأن انتظام مصالح الوقف بإقامة شعائره ليس كانتظامه ببقاء عينه ليقاس عليه ألا ترى إلى ما ذكره المشايخ في توجيه تقديم العمارة على غيرها وإن شرط تأخيرها من قولهم لأنا لو اعتبرنا شرطه أدى ذلك إلى اضمحلال العين الموقوفة فيعود الأمر على ما قصد من الوقف بالإبطال، فقياس الشيخ رحمه الله تعالى الذي ذكره الواقف في الأشباه من تقديم أرباب الشعائر على غيرهم من بقية المستحقين إذا شرط الواقف الاستواء عند الضيق على حكم العمارة قياس مع الفارق ظهوره كالشمس وبعده كاليوم بالنسبة للأمس. هذا وبتقدير تسليمه فالشيخ رحمه الله تعالى قد اختصر عبارة الحاوي وجعلها دليلاً على ما ادعاه مع أن الظاهر من تتمة كلامه ينافي ما ادعاه الشيخ رحمه الله تعالى، وتتمة عبارة الحاوي هو أنه قال بعد ما ذكره الشيخ عنه : هذا إذا لم يكن معيناً، فإن كان الوقف معيناً على شيء يصرف إليه إلا بقدر عمارة البناء اهـ كلام الحاوي. والظاهر هذه التتمة أنها قيد راجع لأصل المسألة فيفيد كلام الحاوي أن تقديم أرباب الشعائر على غيرهم إنما هو في حالة مخصوصة وهي ما إذا لم يعين الواقف قدر ما يعطي لكل مستحق، أما إذا عين لكل قدراً معيناً فلا يصلح أن يكون كلام الحاوي دليلاً على هذا المدعي هذا حاصل ما أفاده المتوقف في كلامه أحيا الله تعالى مذهب إمامه هذا ويمكن أن يجاب عن التوقف الأول بأن يقال المنظور إليه في تقديم أرباب الشعائر على غيرهم من بقية المستحقين ليس هو كونهم كالعمارة من كل وجه وإنما هو من حيثية اشتراكهما في عموم النفع بين العمارة وأرباب الشعائر فلما اشتركا في عموم النفع بالنسبة إلى الغير اشتركا في هذا الحكم وهو تقديمهما على الغير وإن شرط الواقف خلاف ذلك استواء أو تقديم. وإذا تأملت كلام الحاوي القدسي وجدته شاهداً على هذا المدعي. ويجاب عن التوقف الثاني بأن اسم الاشارة الواقع تتمة كلام الحاوي وهو قوله هذا إذا لم يكن معيناً إلى آخره ليس راجعاً لأصل المسألة ليكون قيداً لها وإنما هو راجع لأقرب مذكور في كلامه وهو قوله «تصرف إليهم قدر كفايتهم وكأنه يقول : إن محل تفويض أمر الصرف إلى المتولي إذا لم يشرط الواقف قدراً معيناً لكل مستحق، أما إذا عين فإنه يتبع شرطه. وقد أفصح عن هذا الإمام الزاهدي في كتابه «قنية الفتاوى» حيث قال في باب يحل للمدرس والمتعلم والإمام ما نصه : الأوقاف ببخارى على العلماء لا . ا يعرف من الواقف غير هذا فللقيم أن يفضل البعض ويحرم البعض إذا لم يكن الوقف على قوم يحصون، وكذا الوقف على الذين يختلفون إلى هذه المدرسة أو على متعلميها أو على علمائها يجوز للقيم أن يفضل البعض ويحرم البعض إذا لم يعين الواقف قدر ما يعطي كل واحد اهـ. فهذه العبارة وهي قول صاحب القنية إذا لم يعين الواقف قدر ما يعطي كل واحد أزالت اللبس وأوضحت كل تخمين وحدس . هذا ومما يؤيد ما ذكرناه ما قدمناه من أن المنظور إليه من جهة المعنى في وجه تقديم أرباب الشعائر على غيرهم إنما هو عموم النفع الحاصل من انتظام مصالح المساجد بإقامة شعائرها، وهذا لا يختلف الحال فيه بين ما إذا عين الواقف قدراً معيناً لكل وبين ما إذا لم يعين بخلاف تفويض أمر الصرف للمتولي، فإن غرض الواقف يختلف فيه بينما إذا عين لكل قدراً معيناً وبين ما إذا لم يعين. هذا ما ظهر. قال ذلك وكتبه العبد الفقير الواقف باللطف الخفي قاسم الدنوشري الحنفي في غرة محرم الحرام افتتاح سنة ١١٣٩ والحمد لله وحده، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وآله وصحبه آمين؛ كذا في فتاوى مولانا العلامة حامد أفندي العمادي مفتي دمشق الشام عفا عنه الملك السلام.
Chapter of Waqf. It is said in al-Hawi al-Qudsi from the book of Waqf its wording: 'That which is started with from the proceeds of the endowment is its maintenance, whether stipulated or not, then what is closer to maintenance and more general for benefit, like the imam for the mosque and the teacher for the school, they are given their sufficiency, then the lamp and the mat likewise.' End quote. Our shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said in his book titled al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair from the book of Waqf: 'The apparent meaning of this expression is that those given priority in spending are the imam, teacher, lamplighter, and doorkeeper and those similar to them because of his expression with 'kaaf' (like), and its apparent meaning also indicates the priority of those we mentioned even if the founder stipulated equality when [the revenue] is tight, not making them like maintenance. And if the founder stipulated equality of maintenance with the beneficiaries, his stipulation is not considered, rather maintenance is given priority over them, and likewise them [i.e., these persons].' End quote. What our shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned. So according to what he conveyed that the expression of al-Hawi indicates that the people of rituals are given priority over other beneficiaries and that the stipulation of the founder of equality when tight requires that it be said: the people of rituals are given priority in this endowment asked about, a fortiori, because in the case of stipulating equality of the people of rituals with others, the people of rituals are not completely deprived, and yet the stipulation of equality is nullified. So nullifying it in a case where they might be completely deprived, which is the case of stipulating priority of the people of the two sanctuaries over them, supposing that nothing remains for the people of rituals, is more appropriate. Then some of our shaykhs (may Allah prolong his life) hesitated regarding what our shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) conveyed. The summary of his hesitation is that he said: 'First, we do not accept that the ruling of the people of rituals is analogized to the ruling of maintenance, because the organization of the interests of the endowment by establishing its rituals is not like its organization by preservation of its essence to be analogized to it. Do you not see what the scholars mentioned in justifying giving priority to maintenance over others even if [the founder] stipulated its delay from their saying: we consider his stipulation leads to the destruction of the endowed property, and thus the purpose intended by the endowment would be invalidated. So the analogy of the shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) which the founder mentioned in al-Ashbah of giving priority to the people of rituals over other remaining beneficiaries when the founder stipulated equality at the time of tightness, analogizing it to the ruling of maintenance, is an analogy with a difference, its clarity like the sun, and its distance like today relative to yesterday. And assuming its acceptance, the shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) abbreviated the expression of al-Hawi and made it evidence for his claim, while the apparent meaning of the continuation of his speech contradicts what the shaykh claimed. The continuation of al-Hawi's expression is that he said after what the shaykh mentioned from him: 'This is if it is not specified, but if the endowment is specified for something, it is spent on it except to the extent of maintenance of the building.' End quote of al-Hawi. And apparently this continuation is a restriction referring back to the original issue, so it indicates that giving priority to the people of rituals over others is only in a specific case, i.e., when the founder did not specify the amount to give each beneficiary. But if he specified for each a specific amount, then al-Hawi's words cannot be evidence for this claim.' This is what the one who hesitated conveyed, may Allah revive the madhhab of his imam. And it can be answered regarding the first hesitation by saying: the consideration in giving priority to the people of rituals over other remaining beneficiaries is not that they are like maintenance in every respect, but rather from the aspect of their sharing in general benefit between maintenance and the people of rituals. Since they share in general benefit relative to others, they share in this ruling, which is giving them priority over others even if the founder stipulated otherwise, whether equality or priority. And if you reflect on the words of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, you will find it witness to this claim. And it is answered regarding the second hesitation that the demonstrative pronoun occurring in the continuation of al-Hawi's words, i.e., his saying 'this is if it is not specified' etc., does not refer back to the original issue to be a restriction for it, but rather refers back to the nearest mentioned in his words, i.e., his saying 'they are given their sufficiency'. As if he says: the place of delegation of spending to the trustee is when the founder did not stipulate a specific amount for each beneficiary, but if he specified, then his condition is followed. And this has been clarified by Imam al-Zahidi in his book 'Quniyat al-Fatawa' where he said in the chapter of what is permissible for the teacher, student, and imam, its text: 'Endowments in Bukhara upon scholars... it is not known from the founder other than this, so the administrator may give preference to some and deprive some if the endowment is not upon a countable group. Likewise, the endowment upon those who attend this school or its students or its scholars, it is permissible for the administrator to give preference to some and deprive some if the founder did not specify the amount to give each one.' End quote. This expression, i.e., the statement of the author of Qunyah 'if the founder did not specify the amount to give each one' removed confusion and clarified every conjecture and guess. And what supports what we have mentioned is what we presented earlier that the consideration from the perspective of meaning in the basis of giving priority to the people of rituals over others is the general benefit resulting from the organization of the interests of mosques by establishing their rituals. And this does not differ between when the founder specified a specific amount for each and when he did not, unlike the delegation of spending to the trustee, for the purpose of the founder differs between when he specified for each a specific amount and when he did not. This is what appeared. Said that and wrote it the poor slave, the one who stands by the hidden kindness, Qasim al-Danushari al-Hanafi, in the beginning of Muharram al-Haram, the inauguration of the year 1139. And praise be to Allah alone, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad and his family and companions, Amen. Thus in the Fatawa of our master, the scholar Hamid Efendi al-Imadi, Mufti of Damascus, may the King of Peace forgive him.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the priority of distribution from the proceeds of a waqf when the income is insufficient to cover all stipulated beneficiaries. The discussion centers on whether the imam of a mosque, the mudarris (teacher) of a school, and similar functionaries (like lamplighters and doorkeepers) should be paid before other beneficiaries, even if the waqf founder stipulated equality in distribution. The passage opens with a quote from al-Hawi al-Qudsi, which states that the first priority from waqf revenue is maintenance of the property (whether stipulated or not), then those closest to maintenance and of general benefit, such as the imam and mudarris, who are given their sufficient stipend, then other items like lamps and mats. Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair comments that this implies these functionaries are given priority even against the founder's condition of equality, using an analogy with maintenance: just as maintenance is given priority even if the founder delays it, similarly these functionaries are given priority. An objector challenges this analogy, arguing that the public benefit of rituals is not the same as the preservation of the physical asset; maintenance is necessary to prevent destruction of the waqf, whereas rituals are not. The response defends the analogy by stating that both share in general benefit—just as maintenance benefits all future beneficiaries, the rituals (prayer, teaching) sustain the purpose of the waqf. The objector also points to a continuation in al-Hawi's text that restricts the priority to cases where the founder has not specified fixed amounts for each beneficiary. The response interprets this restriction as pertaining only to the delegation of spending to the trustee, not to the principle of priority. The passage concludes with support from Quniyat al-Fatawa, which confirms that the administrator may give preference when the founder did not specify amounts, reinforcing the idea that priority of functionaries is based on general benefit. A marginal note by Qasim al-Danushari and a reference to the fatawa of Hamid Efendi al-Imadi close the discussion. This ruling is relied upon in the Hanafi school: those whose roles are essential for the waqf's purpose are prioritized over other beneficiaries, and the founder's stipulation of equality at times of shortage is not binding.

Key Terms
أرباب الشعائر (arbāb al-shaʿāʾir): Those who perform the rituals of the mosque/school, i.e., the imam, teacher, lamplighter, doorkeeper, etc., whose roles are essential for the religious and educational functions of the waqf.
قياس مع الفارق (qiyās maʿa al-fāriq): An analogy that is invalid because there is a significant difference between the original case and the new case, making the comparison flawed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, what takes priority in distribution from a waqf with insufficient income?
A) Following the founder's stipulation of equality among all beneficiaries
B) Prioritizing those performing essential rituals (imam, teacher, etc.) even against the founder's condition
C) Distributing equally among all named beneficiaries
D) Returning the income to the founder's heirs

Key Takeaway
Essential waqf functionaries (arbab al-sha'a'ir) are prioritized over other beneficiaries even if the founder stipulated equality, because they provide general benefit akin to maintenance.

Waqf Stipend: Teacher's Attendance and Burden of Proof
Ruling that a teacher's priority in waqf stipend depends on actual attendance and teaching, with fatwa on claims of directorship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a waqf teacher's stipend depends on actual teaching, and apply the evidentiary principle that the teacher's word (with oath) is accepted in disputes.

Core Idea
A teacher's stipend is earned by teaching; if disputed, his word with oath is accepted as a trustee.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key practical question in waqf administration: who is believed when a teacher's performance is disputed? Building on the principle that entitlement to a waqf salary is based on actual work (mubashara), the Hanafi jurists rule that the teacher is a trustee regarding his own work. Therefore, if the overseer denies the teacher taught, the teacher's statement is accepted with an oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the teacher's teaching in a waqf school. The ruling is that the stipend is due only if actual teaching (mubashara) occurred.
Entitlement is not automatic by appointment; it requires performance.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the fatwa of al-Ramli and others, based on the principle that the teacher is an amin (trustee) over his own work.
The argument is aqli (rational) from the nature of trust.
3
Trace the justification
Because the teacher is a trustee, his word is accepted with oath. The overseer's denial or a scribe's report does not outweigh his oath.
This is derived from the general rule that an amin is believed in matters of trust.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion regarding a mosque teacher vs. a school teacher. Al-Maqdisi rejects the distinction, aligning mosque teachers with the same rule.
The mufta bihi is that the rule applies to both.
5
Evaluate the consequence
Consequently, the scribe's attendance record is not accepted as evidence against the teacher's oath. The teacher's and heirs' oaths settle the dispute.
This protects the employee from arbitrary denial by the administrator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : يدرس بعض النهار في مدرسة وبعض النهار في مدرسة أخرى ولا يعلم شرط الواقف يستحق غلة المدرس في المدرستين، ولو كان يدرس بعض الأيام في هذه ثم قال : قوله : (ولكن تقديم المدرس إنما يكون بشرط ملازمته) قال الرملي فلو أنكر الناظر ملازمته فالقول قول المدرس مع يمينه وكذا لو مات واختلف مع ورثته فالقول للورثة مع يمينهم، وقد صرح في فتاوى الشيخ شهاب الدين الحلبي بذلك في وظيفة القراءة بما حاصله : لو شرط القراءة في مصحف بجامع معين وتوفي القارئ والواقف وأنكر من له الولاية على الوقف القراءة المذكورة فالقول قول الورثة في المباشرة مع اليمين لأنهم قائمون مقام مورثهم والقول قوله في المباشرة مع اليمين لأنه أمين فكذلك ورثته .اهـ. أقول : وكذا كل ذي وظيفة القول قوله في المباشرة وهي واقعة الفتوى في مدرس مات وطلب الناظر من ورثته المعلوم المشروط الذي قبضه قبل موته ليرده للوقف لكونه لم يدرس فأفتيت بأن القول قولهم مع اليمين في المباشرة اهـ . وبه يعلم أنه لا يقبل قول كاتب الغيبة وسيأتي توقف المؤلف فيه . قوله : (بخلاف مدرس الجامع) قال المقدسي : أنت خبير بأن ما ذكر لا يشهد لما ادعى من الفرق بين المدرسة والجامع، وغاية ما فيه أن
And in Qunyah: He teaches part of the day in one school and part of the day in another school, and it is not known the condition of the founder, the teacher deserves the produce [stipend] in both schools. And if he used to teach some days in this one, then he said: His statement: (But the teacher's priority is only with the condition of his attendance) al-Ramli said: So if the overseer denies his attendance, the statement is the teacher's statement with his oath. Likewise, if he dies and he differs with his heirs, the statement is the heirs' statement with their oath. And it has been clarified in the Fatawa of Shaykh Shihab al-Din al-Halabi regarding the role of recitation, the conclusion of which: If he stipulated recitation from a specific mushaf in a specific mosque, and the reciter and the founder died, and the one with authority over the waqf denied the mentioned recitation, then the statement is the heirs' statement regarding the directorship with the oath because they stand in the place of their testator, and the statement is his statement regarding the directorship with the oath because he is a trustee, and likewise his heirs. End quote. I say: Likewise, every holder of a role, his statement is accepted regarding the directorship. And this is the actual fatwa regarding a teacher who died, and the overseer asked his heirs to return the known stipulated [salary] which he had taken before his death to give it back to the waqf because he did not teach, so I gave the fatwa that the statement is theirs with the oath regarding the directorship. End quote. And by this it is known that the statement of the attendance scribe is not accepted, and the author's hesitation will come later. His statement: (Unlike the teacher of the mosque) al-Maqdisi said: You are aware that what was mentioned does not witness to what he claimed of the difference between the school and the mosque, and the most it contains is that
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage addresses the condition for a teacher's entitlement to a waqf stipend and the rules of evidence in disputes. It begins with a reference from Qunyah: if a teacher teaches part-time in two schools and the founder's condition is unknown, he is entitled to the stipend from both. Then the commentary examines the matn statement that 'the teacher's priority is only with the condition of his attendance.' Al-Ramli's fatwa states that if the waqf overseer (nazir) denies that the teacher attended, the teacher's own word is accepted (with an oath) because he is a trustee regarding his own work. However, if the teacher dies and the heirs dispute with the overseer, the heirs' word is accepted (with oath) because they stand in their father's place. This is confirmed by a fatwa from Shaykh Shihab al-Din al-Halabi concerning a reciter's role: if the reciter dies and the overseer denies that he performed the recitation, the heirs' word regarding the directorship is accepted. The commentator (the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) adds that this applies to any holder of a waqf role: the person's claim of having performed the work is accepted with oath. He recounts a specific fatwa where a teacher died, and the overseer sought to recover the stipend from the heirs, claiming the teacher had not taught. The fatwa was given that the heirs' word (with oath) is accepted regarding the performance. Consequently, the report of an attendance scribe (katib al-ghayba) is not accepted over the teacher's or heirs' oath, because the scribe is not the one responsible. The passage then addresses the distinction between a teacher of a school (mudarris al-madrasa) and a teacher of a mosque (mudarris al-jami‘); al-Maqdisi criticizes the distinction made by the original text, arguing that the evidence does not support a difference. The text cuts off, but the point is that the principle likely applies to both. The overall ruling is that in disputes about a waqf employee's directorship, the employee's (or his heirs') word is taken with an oath, and the overseer's mere denial or a third-party report is insufficient to overturn that.

Key Terms
المباشرة (al-mubāshara): Direct personal performance of an act, specifically the teacher's actual teaching or reciter's recitation, as opposed to merely being appointed.
كاتب الغيبة (kātib al-ghayba): An attendance scribe who records presence; his report is not accepted as evidence against the teacher's or heirs' oath regarding directorship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf overseer denies that a mudarris actually taught, who is believed according to the fatwa in this passage?
A) The overseer, because he is in charge
B) The teacher, with his oath
C) The attendance scribe's record
D) The students of the teacher

Key Takeaway
In disputes over waqf job performance, the employee's word (with oath) is accepted as a trustee, and the same applies to his heirs after death.

Teacher's Stipend: Attendance and Proportional Payment
Ruling with proof on teacher's stipend and attendance condition in waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the teacher's stipend when attendance is incomplete and apply the rule of proportional payment in waqf disputes.

Core Idea
A teacher's stipend from waqf is proportional to actual work; attendance is a condition for full payment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores a practical waqf issue: what happens when a teacher does not fully meet the attendance condition stipulated by the founder? The Hanafi school applies a principle of fairness — the teacher is paid according to the work actually performed, even if the founder did not specify the exact amount per unit of work. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the burden of proof in disputes with the waqf superintendent, and how this position differs from some Shafi'i views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The passage addresses the teacher's (mudarris) entitlement to a stipend from waqf revenue when the founder stipulated attendance for teaching. What is the condition, and what triggers the entitlement?
The condition is 'mulāzamah' (continuous attendance) at the school for specified days.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on entitlement
The Hanafi position: the teacher is entitled to payment proportional to his actual work. If he taught part of the required time, he receives a corresponding fraction of the stipend. This is derived from istihsan and the principle that the stipulated amount is divided according to work.
This applies even if the founder did not specify the amount per day or per hour.
3
Analyze the burden of proof in disputes
When the superintendent (nāẓir) denies the teacher's attendance, the teacher's word is taken with an oath. Similarly, after the teacher's death, his heirs are believed. This is because the teacher is considered a trustee (amīn) regarding his own work.
The attendance clerk's testimony is not accepted; only the teacher's or heirs' oath matters.
4
Compare with the mosque teacher
The passage distinguishes between a school teacher and a mosque teacher. The school teacher's absence disrupts the school (idle), so attendance is strictly required. The mosque teacher's absence may not cause the same level of disruption. However, the ruling on proportional payment applies equally to both.
The distinction is about the necessity of attendance, not the proportionality of pay.
5
Examine the inter-madhhab difference
Some Shafi'is (Ibn al-Subki) hold that if the amount of work is unknown, the teacher deserves nothing because the contract is ambiguous. The Hanafi response: istihsan supports giving a fair wage for actual work, and this is the relied-upon view.
The practical difference: Hanafi teachers receive partial payment; Shafi'i teachers get nothing if work unspecified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It is as if he says: the place of delegating the matter of spending to the trustee is when the waqf founder did not specify a set amount for each beneficiary. If he specified, then his condition is followed. Imam al-Zahidi has clarified this in his book Quniat al-Fatawa, where he said in the chapter on what is permissible for the teacher, learner, and imam, the text of which is: The endowments of Bukhara for scholars, nothing other than this is known from the founder. So the custodian may prefer some and deprive others if the endowment is not for a countable group. Likewise, the endowment for those who attend this school or for its students or for its scholars, it is permissible for the custodian to prefer some and deprive others if the founder did not specify the amount to give each one. End quote. So this statement - the author of al-Qunyah's statement 'if the founder did not specify the amount to give each one' - removed confusion and clarified every conjecture and guess. And among what supports what we have mentioned is what we previously presented: that the consideration in terms of meaning in giving precedence to those in charge of rituals over others is only the general benefit obtained from organizing the interests of mosques by establishing their rituals. This does not differ in situation between when the founder specified a set amount for each and when he did not, unlike delegating the matter of spending to the trustee, for the founder's objective differs between when he specified a set amount for each and when he did not. This is apparent. Said and written by the poor slave relying on the hidden kindness of Allah, Qasim al-Danushuri al-Hanafi, at the beginning of Muharram al-Haram, the opening of the year 1139. All praise is due to Allah alone, and may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions, Amen. Likewise in the fatwas of our master, the scholar Hamid Efendi al-'Imadi, mufti of Damascus, may the Sovereign of Peace forgive him. His statement: (But the teacher is given priority only with the condition of his attendance.) Al-Ramli said: If the superintendent denies his attendance, the saying is the teacher's saying with his oath. Likewise if he dies and disputes with his heirs, the saying is the heirs' saying with their oath. And Shaykh Shihab al-Din al-Halabi has stated in his fatwas regarding the function of reading, the summary of which: If reading in a specific mosque's mushaf was stipulated, and the reader and founder died, and the one who has authority over the endowment denies the aforementioned reading, the saying is the heirs' saying regarding the performance with the oath because they stand in the place of their testator. And the saying is his regarding the performance with the oath because he is trustworthy, likewise his heirs. End quote. I say: And likewise every functionary, the saying is his regarding the performance. The fatwa case was regarding a teacher who died and the superintendent demanded from his heirs the known stipulated amount that he had taken before his death to return it to the endowment because he did not teach. I issued a fatwa that the saying is theirs with the oath regarding the performance. End quote. From this, it is known that the statement of the attendance clerk is not accepted. The author's hesitation will come later. His statement: (Unlike the teacher of the Friday mosque.) Al-Maqdisi said: You are aware that what has been mentioned does not support the claimed distinction between the school and the mosque. At most, it is that the school and some of it in the other does not entitle him to the full stipend from both. The ruling for the learner and teacher in both cases is the same. End quote. It is understood from his statement 'does not entitle him to the full stipend from both' that he is entitled according to his work. This is very common among job holders in our time. The conclusion is that one looks at what the founder stipulated for him and the work required of him, and the stipulated amount is divided according to his work, contrary to some Shafi'is, for they say: If the stipulated work is not known, he is not entitled to anything from the stipulated amount, as mentioned by Ibn al-Subki.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on the matn. The main issue is the condition for the teacher (mudarris) to receive his stipend from waqf. The text first addresses a condition that is not considered, then establishes that the teacher's priority for stipend is conditional upon his actual attendance at the school for teaching on the specified days each week. This is because if the teacher is absent, the school becomes idle, unlike the teacher of a Friday mosque. The text then cites al-Qunyah to discuss a scenario where the teacher teaches part-time in two schools and whether he deserves the full stipend from both. The key principle is that if the waqf founder did not specify the amount, the trustee may differentiate among beneficiaries; if he did specify, the condition is followed. The passage includes a fatwa from Hamid Efendi al-'Imadi and al-Ramli regarding the burden of proof when the superintendent (nazir) denies the teacher's attendance: the teacher's word is taken with an oath, and likewise his heirs after death. The text then compares the madrasa teacher with the mosque teacher, concluding that they are similar in that the stipend is proportional to actual work. Finally, a dispute with some Shafi'is is noted: the Shafi'is hold that if the stipulated work amount is unknown, no payment is due, whereas the Hanafis say payment is given proportionally. This is a clear inter-madhhab difference. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that the teacher's word is taken regarding performance, and he is paid according to his actual work when the amount is not specified.

Key Terms
مدرس (mudarris): Teacher in a school (madrasa) appointed via waqf; entitled to stipend from waqf revenue.
ملازمة (mulāzamah): Continuous attendance or association; here the condition that the teacher must regularly attend the school to teach.
ناظر (nāẓir): Superintendent or trustee of the waqf, responsible for managing its affairs and paying beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a waqf superintendent denies that a teacher attended his classes, whose word is taken?
A) The superintendent's word
B) The teacher's word with an oath
C) The word of the attendance clerk
D) The word of the neighbors

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi waqf law, a teacher's stipend is proportional to actual work performed, and in disputes, the teacher's word is taken with an oath.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
12 min
Order of Priority in Waqf Expenditures
Specifying the order of priority for spending waqf revenue on mosque staff and supplies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi priority order for spending waqf revenue on mosque staff and supplies, and identify which roles are considered sha'air.

Core Idea
Waqf spending must prioritize essential religious functions: after building, imam, teacher, then lamp and carpet.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the hierarchy of expenditures from waqf revenues for a mosque. The trustee (qayyim) must follow this order to ensure that the mosque's religious functions (sha'air) are sustained. Misallocation can lead to the mosque losing its purpose and the trustee being liable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Understand that after maintaining the mosque building itself, the next priority is spending on the 'rituals' (sha'air) — the personnel and items essential for religious functions.
The building maintenance is always first; the text assumes that is already done.
2
List the specific sha'air in order
From the text, the order is: imam (includes khatib), teacher (mudarris), then fire-tender and floor-spreader, then muezzin and superintendent, and then lamp oil, carpets, and water for ablution.
The word 'then' (ثم) indicates sequence.
3
Identify what is not sha'air
The text explicitly excludes: the direct overseer (mubashir), witness (shahid), collector (jabi), shadd (announcer), and librarian (khazin al-kutub). These are not part of the essential rituals.
Despite common practice in Egypt, the text says this is not Shar'i.
4
Recognize doubtful cases and exceptions
The doorman (bauwab) and water carrier (muzammilati) are subject to doubt; later authorities include them. Also, if a waqf is specifically for the imam, it cannot be diverted. Excess spending on lamps in Ramadan is waste and innovation.
These nuanced rulings show the importance of the founder's conditions and preventing extravagance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله «ثم السراج» بكسر السين أي القناديل ومراده مع زيتها . والبساط - بكسر الباء - أي الحصير ويلحق بهما معلوم خادمها وهو الوقاد والفراش فيقدمان. وتعبيره بـ ثم دون الواو يدل على أنهما مؤخران عن الإمام والمدرس. وفي القنية : لو اشترى بساطاً نفيساً من غلته جاز إذا استغنى المسجد عن العمارة اهـ. وقوله «إلى آخر المصالح» أي مصالح المسجد فيدخل المؤذن والناظر لأنا قدمنا أنهم من المصالح، وقدمنا أن الخطيب داخل تحت الإمام لأنه إمام الجامع فتحصل أن الشعائر التي تقدم في الصرف مطلقاً بعد العمارة الإمام والخطيب والمدرس والوقاد والفراش والمؤذن والناظر وثمن القناديل والزيت والحصر، ويلحق بثمن الزيت والحصر ثمن ماء الوضوء أو أجرة حمله أو كلفة نقله من البئر إلى الميضأة فليس المباشر والشاهد والجابي والشاد وخازن الكتب من الشعائر، وقد جرت العادة بمصر في ديوان المحاسبة بتقديمهم مع المذكورين أولاً وليس شرعياً، ويقع الاشتباه في البواب والمزملاتي . وفي الخانية : لو جعل حجرته لدهن سراج المسجد ولم يزد صارت وقفاً على المسجد إذا سلمها إلى المتولي وعليه الفتوى، وليس للمتولي أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن اهـ . فعلى هذا الموقوف على إمام للمسجد لا يصرف لغيره. وفي الخانية : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لأعمال البر هل يجوز أن يسرج المسجد منه؟ قال الفقيه أبو بكر: يجوز ولا يجوز أن يزاد على سراج المسجد لأن ذلك إسراف، سواء كان ذلك في رمضان أو غيره، ولا يزين المسجد بهذه الوصية .اهـ. ومقتضاه منع الكثرة الواقعة في رمضان في مساجد القاهرة ولو شرط الواقف لأن شرطه لا يعتبر في المعصية. وفي القنية : وإسراج السرج الكثيرة في السكك والأسواق ليلة البراءة بدعة، وكذا في المساجد ويضمن القيم، وكذا الجامع الذي شرط فيه تدريس إذا غاب مدرسه لم يقطع من حيث كونه جامعاً ويتعطل من حيث كونه مدرسة فيجب تقديمه من هذه الحيثية. قوله : (والشاد) قيل هو الدعجي، قلت: ويشهد له ما في القاموس : الإشادة رفع الصوت بالشيء وتعريف الضالة والإهلال والشياد الدعاء بالإبل وذلك الطيب بالجلد. قوله : ( ويقع الاشتباه في البواب والمزملاتي قال في الدر المنتقى : المزملاتي هو الشاوي بعرف أهل الشام . وذكر الشرنبلالي في شرح الوهبانية أن ظهور شمول تقديم البواب والمزملاتي وخادم المطهرة مما لا يتردد فيه اهـ. قوله : (وليس للمتولى أن يصرف الغلة إلى غير الدهن) سيأتي لهذا زيادة في
His statement: 'Then the lamp' – with kasra on the sin, meaning the lanterns (qanadil) and he intends with their oil. And 'the carpet' – with kasra on the ba, meaning the mat (hasir). Attached to them is the wage of its servant, who is the fire-tender and the floor-spreader, so they are given precedence. His expression with 'thumma' instead of 'waw' indicates that they are after the imam and the teacher. In al-Qunyah: If he buys a precious carpet from its revenue, it is permissible if the mosque is not in need of repair. End quote. His statement: 'to the end of the interests' – meaning the interests of the mosque, so it includes the muezzin and the superintendent, because we previously stated that they are from the interests. And we previously stated that the khatib is included under the imam because he is the imam of the Friday mosque. So the outcome is that the rituals (sha'air) that are given precedence in spending absolutely, after building maintenance, are: the imam, khatib, teacher, fire-tender, floor-spreader, muezzin, and superintendent, plus the price of lanterns, oil, and mats. Attached to the price of oil and mats is the price of water for ablution, or the wage of carrying it, or the cost of transporting it from the well to the place of ablution. So the direct overseer (mubashir), witness (shahid), collector (jabi), shadd (tashid), and librarian (khazin al-kutub) are not from the rituals. In Egypt, the custom in the accounting department has been to give them precedence along with those mentioned first, but this is not legal. Doubt arises regarding the doorman (bauwab) and the muzammilati (water carrier). In al-Khaniyya: If someone makes his room for the oil of the mosque lamp and does not increase, it becomes an endowment for the mosque if he hands it over to the trustee, and the fatwa is upon this. The trustee cannot spend the revenue on anything other than oil. End quote. Based on this, what is endowed for an imam of the mosque cannot be spent on other than him. In al-Khaniyya: A man bequeathed a third of his wealth for charitable deeds. Is it permissible to provide lamps for the mosque from it? The faqih Abu Bakr said: It is permissible, but it is not permissible to exceed the usual mosque lighting because that is wastefulness, whether in Ramadan or otherwise. The mosque should not be decorated with this bequest. End quote. Its implication prevents the excessive (lamps) occurring in Ramadan in the mosques of Cairo, even if the waqf founder stipulated it, because his stipulation is not considered in sin. In al-Qunyah: Lighting many lamps in alleys and markets on the Night of Bara'ah is an innovation. Likewise in mosques, and the custodian is liable. Also the Friday mosque in which teaching was stipulated, if its teacher is absent, it does not cease to be a Friday mosque, but from the perspective of being a school it becomes idle, so he should be given precedence from this perspective. His statement: (And the shadd – it is said it is the announcer (da'aji). I say: What supports this is in al-Qamus: al-ishada is raising the voice with something and announcing a lost item and raising the voice in talbiya; and al-shiyad is calling camels; and the pleasant smell on leather. His statement: 'And doubt arises regarding the doorman and the muzammilati.' In al-Durr al-Muntaqa: Al-muzammilati is the seller of grilled meat in the terminology of the people of Sham. Al-Shurunbalali mentioned in Sharh al-Wahbaniyya that the clarity of the inclusion of the doorman, the muzammilati, and the servant of the water place is not to be hesitated about. End quote. His statement: 'And the trustee cannot spend the revenue on other than oil' – more on this will follow.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the order of priorities in spending waqf revenue. The text begins by explaining that the 'lamp' and 'carpet' are given after the imam and teacher (mudarris). The word 'then' (ثم) indicates this order. Then it defines 'lamp' as the lanterns with their oil, and 'carpet' as the mat. Attached to these are the wages of the fire-tender and floor-spreader. A quote from al-Qunyah allows purchasing a precious carpet if the mosque is not in need of repair. The text then broadens to 'all interests of the mosque', which includes the muezzin and nazir, and notes that the khatib is included under the imam. The complete list of 'rituals' (sha'air) that are given priority after building maintenance is: imam, khatib, mudarris, fire-tender, floor-spreader, muezzin, nazir, plus the price of lanterns, oil, and mats. Also attached are costs for water for ablution. Notably, the mubashir, shahid, jabi, shadd, and khazin al-kutub are not considered part of the rituals, though customary practice in Egypt put them forward, which the text notes is not Shar'i. Doubt arises regarding the doorman (bauwab) and the muzammilati (water carrier). The text then cites al-Khaniyya on a specific case: if a person made his room specifically for mosque lamp oil, it becomes a valid waqf and the trustee cannot divert the revenue to other uses. Similarly, a bequest for charitable deeds can be used for mosque lighting but not excessively, and the Night of Bara'ah practice of lighting many lamps is considered innovation (bid'ah) and the custodian is liable. The passage also mentions the definition of 'shadd' as an announcer, and ends with the note that the trustee cannot spend oil revenue elsewhere.

Key Terms
شعائر (sha'ā'ir): Rituals or religious functions of the mosque; specifically the personnel and items necessary for the mosque to operate, such as imam, teacher, lamp, etc.
قيم (qayyim): Custodian or supervisor of the waqf, responsible for managing and spending revenues according to the founder's conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT considered part of the 'sha'air' (rituals) that should be given priority in waqf spending?
A) Imam and teacher
B) Lamp oil and carpet
C) The direct overseer (mubashir)
D) Muezzin and superintendent

Key Takeaway
After building maintenance, the Hanafi priority for waqf spending is: imam, khatib, teacher, fire-tender, floor-spreader, muezzin, superintendent, lamp oil, carpet, and water; other staff like overseer and librarian are not given this priority.
